Entering Mecca Without Ihram: Obligation, Dispute, and Tadakhul
Explaining obligations and disputes regarding entering Mecca without ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering Mecca without ihram, explain the dispute with al-Shafi'i, and apply the principle of tadakhul to determine when a single hajj suffices for multiple obligations.

Core Idea
Entering Mecca without ihram obligates a ritual; one hajj in the same year can interlock to cover that obligation.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the Hanafi position on entering Mecca without ihram. It establishes that any person from beyond the miqat (āfāqī) who enters Mecca—whether for hajj, umrah, trade, or any other purpose—must perform one of the two rituals. The ruling is contested by al-Shafi'i, who permits entry without ihram if no ritual is intended. Additionally, the passage introduces the concept of tadakhul (interlocking), whereby a hajj performed in the same year as the entry fulfills the obligation, even without a separate intention. This principle is based on istihsan and analogized to a vowed retreat fulfilled by the Ramadan fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the obligation
A person from beyond the miqat (e.g., a Kufi) enters Mecca without ihram for any reason. In Hanafi fiqh, this immediately makes hajj or umrah obligatory, because entry itself is a sabab (cause) for ihram as an act of veneration.
The obligation is not dependent on intention; it applies even if one enters for trade or visitation.
2
Examine the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that entry without ihram is permissible if one does not intend a ritual, since the original state is permissibility. The Hanafi position is that the sanctity of Mecca demands ihram as a precondition for entry.
This dispute has practical consequences: a Shafi'i trader may enter Mecca without ihram, while a Hanafi trader must later perform hajj/umrah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof and the concept of tadakhul
The passage analogizes the obligation to a vowed retreat (i'tikāf): just as a Ramadan fast fulfills a vowed retreat without a separate intention, similarly, performing hajj in the same year as the entry cancels the obligation via tadakhul. This is based on istihsan, overriding the qiyas of Zufar.
Zufar argues that the obligation becomes a debt (dayn) requiring specific intention, so tadakhul is invalid. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) accept tadakhul.
4
Determine when tadakhul applies
Tadakhul only applies if the hajj (or umrah) is performed in the same year as the entry. If the year passes, the obligation becomes a debt and cannot be fulfilled by a later hajj without a new intention.
This is similar to the vowed retreat: fasting in Ramadan of the same year fulfills it, but not if the year passes.
5
Apply to a concrete case
Take a person who enters Mecca without ihram in Muharram and then performs hajj in Dhul-Hijjah of the same year. The hajj covers both the hajj of Islam (if applicable) and the obligation from the entry. If he delays hajj until the next year, it does not cover the entry obligation.
The key is the 'same year' condition; multiple entries also incur multiple obligations, but a single hajj only covers the last entry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مجاوزة الوقت بغير إحرام
فلو دخل الكوفي البستان الحاجة له دخول مكة بلا إحرام، ووقته أي الآفاقي البستان، ومن دخل . أي جاز له بطل الدم: [جواب الشرط، أي سقط الدم الذي وجب عليه في المسئلتين. (ط، ع)] أي في هذه الصورة أيضاً، وهي إذا جاوز ثم أحرم بعمرة ثم أفسد العمرة وقضاها بإحرام من الميقات، وعند زفر: لا يسقط في هذه الصورة أيضاً؛ لأنه بالعود لا ترتفع الجناية، ولنا أنه تلافى المتروك بالقضاء من الميقات فانجبر ذلك النقصان. (فتح) فلو دخل الكوفي نبه بهذا التفريع على أن ما مر من لزوم الإحرام من الميقات إنما هو على من قصد أحد النسكين أو دخول مكة أو الحرم، فقصد مكة أو الحرم موجب له، سواء قصد نسكاً أو لا، أما إذا قصد مكاناً من الحل داخل الميقات، فإنه لا يجوز له الدخول لالتحاقه بأهله، سواء نوى الإقامة الشرعية أي خمسة عشر يوماً أو لم ينو، وعن أبي يوسف: إن نوى الإقامة أقل من خمسة عشر يوماً لا يكون منهم، فلا يكون له أن يدخل مكة بغير إحرام والحاصل أن من كان دون الميقات له دخول مكة بلا إحرام سواء قصد حاجة بالبستان عند دخوله أم لا، وليس المراد بالكوفي خصوصه، بل أراد به الآفاقي كوفياً كان أم لا، ولو أحرم من البستان للحج ولم يدخل مكة حتى وقف بعرفة أجزأه؛ لأنه أحرم من ميقاته ولم يترك نسكاً واجباً، فلا يلزمه شيء كأهل البستان. (عيني، فتح) البستان: أي بستان بني عامر، وهي قرية في داخل الميقات وخارج الحرم، تسمى الآن نخلة وعشرون ميلاً من مكة رمز الحقائق: ۱۸۲/۱] لحاجة عرضت له أي لا لدخول مكة ثم بدا له أن يدخل. (ط ، ع ) بلا إحرام لأنه التحق بأهل البستان، و للبستاني أن يدخل مكة بلا إحرام للحاجة، فكذا له عيني ووقته أي ميقاته إذا أراد الإحرام. (ع) البستان أراد جميع الحل الذي بينه وبين الحرم كالبستاني. [رمز الحقائق: ۱۸۲/۱] ومن دخل إلخ : أي يجب عليه أحد النسكين لكل دخول، ثم إذا في عامه ذلك حج صح من دخوله مكة، يعني من أخر دخوله بغير إحرام؛ فإنه لو دخلها مرارا وجب عليه لكل مرة حجة أو عمرة، فإذا خرج فأحرم بنسك أجزأه عن آخر دخوله لا عما له قبله؛ لأن الواجب قبل الإحرام صار دينا في ذمته فلا يسقط إلا بالنية، والغرض أنه إذا دخل كوفي مكة بلا إحرام لحاجة له يجب عليه عمرة أو حجة، إن كانت في وقتها، خلافا للشافعي بناء على أن له أن يدخل مكة بغير إحرام إن لم يرد أحد النسكين عنده وعندنا: ليس له ذلك، فإن رجع إلى الميقات فأهل بحجة الإسلام وعما لزمه بدخوله مكة بطريق التداخل، وفي القياس لا يجوز وهو قول زفر؛ لأنه بدخول وجب عليه حجة أو عمرة وصار ذلك دينا في ذمته، فلا يتأدى إلا بالنية ولنا أنه تلافي المتروك في وقته؛ لأن الواجب عليه تعظيم هذه البقعة بالإحرام كما إذا أتاها بحجة الإسلام في الابتداء، وصار كالاعتكاف المنذور؛ فإنه يتأدى بصوم رمضان. (مستخلص، فتح)

مكة

مكة بلا إحرام ثم حجّ مما عليه في عامه ذلك صح من دخول مكة بلا إحرام، فإن تحولت السنة لا .
أي هذه
عما لزمه
بلا إحرام حتى وجب عليه أحد النسكين يعني الحج والعمرة؛ لأن دخوله سبب لوجوب الإحرام، سواء قصد الحج أو العمرة أو التجارة، أو لم يقصد شيئاً. (ط،ع)
مما عليه: أي مما وجب عليه من حجة الإسلام أو حجة منذورة أو عمرة منذورة. (ط،ع)
فإن تحولت السنة لا: أي إذا تحولت السنة ثم أحرم بالحج من الميقات لا ينوب عما وجب عليه بدخول مكة بلا إحرام؛ لأنه لما تحولت السنة صار ما وجب بدخول مكة بلا إحرام دينا في ذمته، فلا يتأدى إلا بإحرام كما في اعتكاف المنذور في رمضان من هذه السنة؛ فإنه يتأدى بصوم رمضان من هذه السنة دون العام المقصود الثاني. (مستخلص)
Book of Hajj
Passing the time without ihram
If a Kufi enters the garden [Bustan] needing to enter Mecca without ihram, and its time [i.e., the miqat of the horizon person, the garden], and whoever enters... meaning it is permitted for him. The blood sacrifice is nullified: [response of the condition, i.e., the blood that was obligated in the two cases falls away. (T, A)] i.e., in this scenario as well, which is when he passed [the miqat] then assumed ihram for umrah, then corrupted the umrah and made it up with ihram from the miqat. According to Zufar: it does not fall away in this scenario either because with the return the offense is not removed. For us: he has made up the omission by completing it from the miqat, so that deficiency is compensated. (Fath)
So if the Kufi entered... he points by this detail to what passed about the obligation of ihram from the miqat is only upon one who intends one of the two rituals or entering Mecca or the Haram. So intending Mecca or the Haram necessitates it, whether he intends a ritual or not. But if he intends a place within the non-sanctuary inside the miqat, then he is not permitted to enter [Mecca] because he joins his family, whether he intends legal residence—i.e., fifteen days—or not. From Abu Yusuf: if he intends residence less than fifteen days, he is not from them, so he may not enter Mecca without ihram. The conclusion: whoever is within the miqat may enter Mecca without ihram, whether he intends a need in the garden at his entry or not. What is meant by 'Kufi' is not specific, but he intends the horizon person, whether Kufi or not. And if he assumes ihram from the garden for hajj and does not enter Mecca until he stands at Arafah, it suffices because he assumed ihram from his miqat and did not omit an obligatory ritual, so nothing is required of him like the people of the garden. (Ayni, Fath)
The garden: i.e., Bustan Bani Amir, which is a village inside the miqat and outside the Haram, now called Nakhlah, twenty miles from Mecca. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 182/1] For a need that occurs to him, i.e., not for entering Mecca, then he decides to enter. (T, A) Without ihram because he joins the people of the garden. And the gardener may enter Mecca without ihram for need, so likewise for him. (Ayni) And its time, i.e., his miqat when he wants to assume ihram. (A) The garden intended all the non-sanctuary area between it and the Haram like the gardener. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 182/1]
'And whoever enters' etc.: i.e., one of the two rituals is obligatory for each entry. Then if in that same year he performs hajj, it is valid from his entry into Mecca, meaning he delayed his entry without ihram. If he enters repeatedly, a hajj or umrah is obligated for each time. If he then goes out and assumes ihram for a ritual, it suffices for his last entry, not for what preceded it, because the obligation before ihram becomes a debt in his liability and is not removed except by intention. The point is that if a Kufi enters Mecca without ihram for a need, a umrah or hajj is obligatory upon him, if it is in its time, contrary to al-Shafi'i, based on the view that he may enter Mecca without ihram if he does not intend one of the two rituals according to him. According to us: he does not have that right. If he returns to the miqat and raises his voice for the hajj of Islam and for what is required by his entry into Mecca via interlocking, according to qiyas it is not permitted, and that is Zufar's statement, because by entry a hajj or umrah becomes obligatory, and that becomes a debt in his liability, so it is not fulfilled except by intention. For us: it is making up the omission in its time because what is obligatory upon him is veneration of this place through ihram, just as if he came with the hajj of Islam initially, and it becomes like a vowed retreat; for it is fulfilled by the fast of Ramadan. (Mukhtalaf, Fath)

Mecca

Mecca without ihram, then he performs hajj from what is upon him in that same year, it is valid from his entry into Mecca without ihram. Then if the year passes, no.

without ihram until one of the two rituals became obligatory, meaning hajj and umrah, because his entry is a cause for the obligation of ihram, whether he intends hajj or umrah or trade, or intends nothing. (T, A)
From what is upon him: i.e., from what became obligatory upon him of the hajj of Islam, or a vowed hajj, or a vowed umrah. (T, A)
Then if the year passes, no: i.e., if the year passes and then he assumes ihram for hajj from the miqat, it does not substitute for what became obligatory upon him by entering Mecca without ihram, because when the year passed, what became obligatory by entering Mecca without ihram became a debt in his liability, so it is not fulfilled except by ihram, as in the case of a vowed retreat in Ramadan of this year; for it is fulfilled by the fast of Ramadan in this year, not the following year. (Mukhtalaf)
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with the ruling for a person who passes the miqat without ihram and then enters Mecca. The passage type is an inter-madhhab dispute combined with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The author first discusses the case of a Kufi (a person from the east of the miqat) who enters the Bustan (a village inside the miqat) for a need and then enters Mecca without ihram. Initially, a blood sacrifice (dam) is required. However, if he then returns to the miqat, assumes ihram for umrah, corrupts that umrah, and makes it up by a new ihram from the miqat, the dam is cancelled. This is because he has compensated for the omission. Zufar disagrees, arguing the return does not remove the offense. The Hanafi position is that the compensation suffices.

Next, the commentary explains that the obligation of ihram from the miqat applies to anyone who intends either hajj/umrah or simply entering Mecca or the Haram. If one intends a place outside the Haram but inside the miqat, he may enter Mecca without ihram only if he is joining his family (i.e., he is a resident of that area). This is based on the ruling for the 'gardener' (resident of the Bustan) who may enter Mecca for a need without ihram. Abu Yusuf adds a condition regarding intention of residence (15 days or more). The point is that the term 'Kufi' is not literal; it refers to any horizon person.

Then the passage addresses the general rule: whoever enters Mecca without ihram must perform a hajj or umrah for each entry. If he enters multiple times, each entry incurs an obligation. If he then performs a hajj or umrah, it only covers the last entry, not previous ones, because the earlier obligations became a debt in his liability and need specific intention. This is contrary to al-Shafi'i, who permits entering Mecca without ihram if one does not intend a ritual. The Hanafi position is that it is not permitted.

Finally, the passage discusses whether performing the hajj of Islam in the same year as the entry suffices for the obligation incurred by the entry. According to the Hanafi school, if he performs hajj from what is upon him (e.g., hajj of Islam or a vowed hajj) in that same year, it covers that obligation due to interlocking (tadakhul). This is based on istihsan, not qiyas (which Zufar follows). However, if the year passes, the obligation becomes a debt and cannot be fulfilled by a later hajj without a new intention, similar to a vowed retreat in Ramadan: if one fasts Ramadan, it covers the vowed retreat in that same year, but not in a later year.

Key Terms
البستان (al-Bustan): Bustan Bani Amir, a village inside the miqat and outside the Haram, about 20 miles from Mecca.
الآفاقي (al-āfāqī): A person coming from beyond the miqat, whether from Kufa or any other distant land.
التداخل (al-tadākhul): The interlocking of obligations where a single act fulfills multiple duties simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person from beyond the miqat enters Mecca without ihram for trade, what is required?
A) Nothing, as he did not intend a ritual.
B) A blood sacrifice (dam) only.
C) A hajj or umrah to be performed in the same year if possible.
D) He must leave Mecca immediately.

Key Takeaway
Entering Mecca without ihram obligates a hajj or umrah; the obligation can be fulfilled by a same-year hajj via tadakhul.

Ruling on Entering Mecca without Ihram and Performing Hajj in the Same Year
States ruling for one who exceeds miqat without ihram and performs Hajj same year.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a person who enters Mecca without ihram and then performs Hajj in the same year, and explain the consequence if the year passes without performance.

Core Idea
Entering Mecca without ihram triggers an obligation that must be fulfilled in the same year.

This lesson from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a scenario where a person passes the miqat (the boundary for ihram) without entering the state of ihram and then later performs Hajj within the same year. The passage clarifies whether such a Hajj is valid and what happens if the year elapses without performance. Understanding this ruling is important because it affects the validity of one's Hajj and the nature of the obligation incurred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is entering Mecca (passing the miqat) without ihram. The ruling is that it becomes obligatory to perform either Hajj or Umrah in the same year. If performed, the act is valid (sahih) and fulfills the obligation.
The obligation is triggered by merely passing the boundary, regardless of intention.
2
Note the time bound
The performance must occur within the same Islamic year. If done, it suffices. If not, the obligation becomes a debt (dayn) in the person's liability.
The year here refers to the lunar year.
3
Understand the consequence of delay
If the year passes and then the person performs Hajj from the miqat, that later Hajj does not substitute for the debt. He must perform a separate act specifically for that obligation.
The analogy with a vowed i'tikaf in Ramadan is used: fasting that Ramadan fulfills it, but not the next year's fast.
4
Recognize the scope of the cause
The obligation arises whether the person intended Hajj, Umrah, trade, or nothing at all. Entering Mecca itself is the cause (sabab).
This is a general ruling; intention does not affect the obligation.
5
Apply the analogy for deeper understanding
The text compares this to a vowed i'tikaf in Ramadan: like fasting that Ramadan fulfills the vow, performing Hajj in the same year fulfills the obligation. After the year, a new separate act is needed.
This analogy helps remember the time-bound nature.

But if the year passes, no. Meaning: [the obligation] from what he owes. Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the ruling on a person who passes the miqat without entering ihram and then performs Hajj in the same year. The author states that if such a person enters Mecca without ihram, he must perform either Hajj or Umrah that same year. If he does so, his action is valid and fulfills the obligation incurred by entering without ihram. However, if the year passes without him performing it, the obligation becomes a debt on his conscience, and subsequent performance of Hajj from the miqat will not count for that debt. The commentary explains that the cause for obligation is simply entering Mecca, regardless of intention. The analogy with i'tikaf clarifies that like a vowed i'tikaf in Ramadan can be fulfilled by fasting that Ramadan, but not in the next year, similarly, the Hajj performance in the same year fulfills the obligation, but after the year, a new separate act is needed.

Key Terms
مجاوزة الوقت (mujāwazat al-waqt): The act of passing the miqat (boundary for ihram) without entering the state of ihram.
إحرام (iḥrām): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, consisting of intention and talbiyah.
نسكين (nusukayn): The two rituals: Hajj and Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He is free of obligation.
D) He must perform Umrah only.

Key Takeaway
Entering Mecca without ihram obligates a person to perform Hajj or Umrah within the same year; after the year, the obligation becomes a debt that a later Hajj cannot fulfill.

Adding Hajj to Umrah: The Makkan's Dilemma and Hanafi Dispute
Discusses ruling for a Makkan who adds Hajj ihram after some Umrah tawaf, with Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on which ihram a Makkan should abandon when adding Hajj after partial Umrah, and state the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When a Makkan adds Hajj after partial Umrah, Abu Hanifa abandons Hajj; Sahibayn abandon Umrah.

The ruling for a Makkan who adds Hajj ihram after performing some tawaf for Umrah is not unanimous within the Hanafi school. Abu Hanifa holds that the more confirmed Umrah ihram should be retained, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue the opposite, citing the relative ease of making up Umrah. This lesson unpacks their proofs and the practical consequences of each view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and identify the dispute
The matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) rules that a Makkan who does one tawaf for Umrah then adds Hajj should abandon the Hajj. This is Abu Hanifa's view. But the Sahibayn disagree: they hold that the Umrah should be abandoned.
2
Follow the reasoning of each party
Abu Hanifa argues that the Umrah ihram is confirmed by the performed tawaf, making it stronger; the less confirmed (Hajj) should be abandoned. The Sahibayn argue that Umrah is lesser in acts, non-time-bound, and easier to make up, so it should be abandoned.
3
Identify when there is consensus
If the Makkan performed four circuits for Umrah before adding Hajj, all agree to abandon Hajj. If no Umrah acts were performed, all agree to abandon Umrah.
These consensus points show the boundary of the dispute.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa: he abandons Hajj, completes Umrah, then must perform both Hajj and Umrah the next year with a sacrifice. Under Sahibayn: he abandons Umrah, continues with Hajj, and only makes up Umrah later.
The difference affects how many qada acts and sacrifices are required.

(عيني، فتح)
أفعال
Chapter on Adding Ihram to Ihram, i.e., explaining its ruling. A Makkan who performed one circuit for Umrah and then entered ihram for Hajj: he abandons it (the Hajj), and upon him is a Hajj and Umrah and a blood sacrifice for his abandonment. (Meaning after the ihram for Umrah) next year. Chapter on Adding Ihram etc.: The meaning of adding ihram is entering it upon the other ihram. (Al-Muhashi) Addition for the Makkan and whoever is inside the miqats is an offense (jinaayah) unlike the afaaqi, except in adding the ihram of Umrah in Hajj; by the first consideration he mentioned it after the offenses, and by the second he made it a separate chapter. The issues of this chapter, by rational division, are divided into four sections: first: entering Hajj ihram upon Hajj ihram; second: entering Umrah ihram upon Umrah ihram; third: entering Umrah ihram upon Hajj ihram; fourth: entering Hajj ihram upon Umrah ihram. He pointed to the first by his saying: 'Whoever entered ihram for Hajj then entered ihram for another,' and to the second by his saying: 'Whoever finished his Umrah except for the taqsir then entered ihram for another,' and to the third by his saying: 'Whoever entered ihram for Hajj then for Umrah then stood at Arafah,' and to the fourth by his saying: 'A Makkan performed one circuit.' (Fath) 'Performed circuits' – intended is other than the afaaqi, so it includes whoever is inside the miqat as well. (T) He restricted it to the Makkan because the afaaqi does not abandon one of them; rather, if he adds the ihram after performing the minimum circuits, he is a Qarin, otherwise he is a Mutamatti' if that is in the months of Hajj. And he restricted it to Umrah because if he entered ihram for Hajj and performed circuits for it then for Umrah, he would abandon the Umrah by agreement. (Fath) 'One circuit' – intended is the minimum circuits of Umrah, whether one, two, or three. (T) 'He abandons it' – i.e., he must leave the Hajj necessarily by exiting ihram from it by shaving, for example, avoiding sin. (T, Miskin) 'Al-rafd' is abandonment, i.e., abandoning the Hajj, and it should be abandonment by action, such as shaving after completing the acts of Umrah, and it is not sufficient with words or intention. The reason for abandoning it is that combining the two is not legislated for the Makkan. This is according to Abu Hanifah. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: he abandons the Umrah because it is lower in status, fewer in acts, and easier to make up, being non-time-bound, and it only involves tawaf and sa'i, and it is a Sunnah, while Hajj is not. For Abu Hanifah: the ihram for Umrah is confirmed by the circuit he performed, while the ihram for Hajj is not confirmed, and the less confirmed is more deserving of abandonment. Also, abandonment in Umrah is its nullification and invalidation, while in Hajj it is refraining from performance, so it is more appropriate. If he performed four circuits for Umrah, he abandons the Hajj without dispute. Likewise, if he entered ihram for Umrah then for Hajj and did not do anything of Umrah, he abandons the Umrah without dispute. (Ayni, Mustakhlas) 'Upon him is a Hajj and Umrah' – he exits ihram by them because he is like one who missed Hajj, even if he performs it in his year as a make-up, the Umrah is dropped from him. (T) Because he is like a Faa'it al-Hajj, he exits ihram by the acts of Umrah, then performs Hajj the next year, so upon him is a Hajj and Umrah. And his saying: 'and a blood sacrifice for his abandonment' i.e., upon him is a blood sacrifice for abandoning the Hajj, because he was ordered by Aisha to abandon her Umrah with a blood sacrifice, and this blood sacrifice is for exiting ihram before its time. Then if he abandons the Umrah, he only makes it up, and if he abandons the Hajj, he makes it up and also makes up the Umrah. (Ayni, Fath) Acts...
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the rulings on adding one ihram to another, specifically for a Makkan (or someone within the miqat). The matn states: 'A Makkan who performed one circuit (tawaf) for Umrah and then entered into ihram for Hajj should abandon (rafd) the Hajj, and he owes a Hajj and Umrah and a blood sacrifice for the abandonment.' The commentary clarifies that this is the view of Abu Hanifa, who argues that the Umrah ihram has become confirmed by the performance of some tawaf, while the Hajj ihram has not yet been confirmed, so the less confirmed should be abandoned. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the Umrah should be abandoned because it is lesser in status and easier to make up. The text then discusses various scenarios and consensus points: if he performs four circuits, there is no dispute that he abandons Hajj; if he has done nothing of Umrah, he abandons Umrah. The ruling concludes that he must make up both Hajj and Umrah and offer a sacrifice for the premature abandonment.

Key Terms
إضافة الإحرام (iḍāfat al-iḥrām): The act of entering into a second ihram while already in a state of ihram.
رفض (rafḍ): Abandonment; the act of leaving one of the two ihrams, specifically by exiting the state of ihram through actions like shaving.
مكي (makki): A resident of Mecca or anyone within the miqat boundaries.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must abandon the Umrah.
B) He must abandon the Hajj.
C) He can continue both as a qarin.
D) He must perform both separately.

Key Takeaway
When a Makkan adds Hajj after partial Umrah tawaf, Abu Hanifa abandons Hajj; Sahibayn abandon Umrah; the thamarah al-khilaf affects the number of make-up acts and sacrifice.

The Ruling of Adding One Ihram to Another (Idaafat al-Ihram)
Explains the meaning and four categories of adding one ihram to another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of idaafat al-ihram and distinguish when it constitutes a violation (jinaayah) and when it does not.

Core Idea
Adding an ihram is a violation for a Makkan but not for an aafaqi, except in one specific case.

This lesson introduces the concept of adding one ihram to another while still in the first. The Hanafi school distinguishes between residents of Makkah (or those inside the miqat) and outsiders (aafaqi) regarding whether this act is a violation requiring atonement. We will explore the general rule, its exception, and the four possible combinations of adding Hajj or Umrah ihrams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept and its definition
The term 'idaafat al-ihram' means entering a second ihram while already in the first. Recognize that this is the subject of the chapter.
The commentary clarifies that it is 'inserting it upon the other ihram'.
2
Understand the key distinction: Makkan vs. aafaqi
The passage states that adding an ihram is a violation (jinaayah) for a Makkan and those inside the miqat, but not for an aafaqi (one coming from outside). Note the exception: adding the ihram of Umrah in the context of Hajj.
This exception applies to the aafaqi case — it becomes a violation in that specific situation.
3
Learn the four rational categories
The rulings are divided into four categories based on the order and type of ihram: (1) Hajj upon Hajj, (2) Umrah upon Umrah, (3) Umrah upon Hajj, (4) Hajj upon Umrah. The matn alludes to each category through specific examples.
These categories cover all possible combinations of adding one hajj or umrah to another.
4
Connect the categories to the matn allusions
The author (al-Quduri) indicates the first category with 'whoever enters ihram for Hajj then enters another', the second with 'whoever completes his Umrah except for taqsir then enters another', etc.
Each scenario triggers a different ruling depending on whether the person is Makkan or aafaqi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام أي في بيان حكمها × باب إضافة الإحرام إلخ المراد بإضافة الإحرام إدخاله على الإحرام الآخر. (المحشي)] الإضافة في حق المكي ومن هو داخل المواقيت جناية دون الآفاقي، إلا في إضافة إحرام العمرة في الحج، فبالاعتبار الأول ذكره عقب الجنايات، وبالاعتبار الثاني جعله في باب على حدة، ومسائل هذا الباب باعتبار القسمة العقلية تنقسم إلى أربعة أقسام: أولها: أن يدخل إحرام حج على إحرام حج، ثانيها: أن يدخل إحرام العمرة على إحرام العمرة، ثالثها: أن يدخل إحرام عمرة على إحرام حج رابعها أن يدخل إحرام حج على إحرام عمرة، وأشار إلى الأول بقوله: " ومن أحرم بحج ثم أحرم بآخر، وإلى الثاني بقوله: "ومن فرغ من عمرته إلا التقصير فأحرم بأخرى"، وإلى الثالث بقوله: ومن أحرم بحج ثم بعمرة ثم وقف بعرفات"، وإلى الرابع بقوله: "مكي طاف شوطاً". (فتح)
Chapter of adding ihram to ihram, i.e., in explaining its ruling. [Commentary:] The intended meaning of adding ihram is inserting it upon the other ihram. (al-Muhashi) Adding is a violation with respect to a Makkan and whoever is inside the mawaaqeet, not for an aafaqi, except in adding the ihram of Umrah in Hajj. So according to the first consideration, he mentioned it after the violations, and according to the second consideration, he made it in a separate chapter. The rulings of this chapter, according to rational division, are divided into four categories: First: that one enters Hajj ihram upon Hajj ihram. Second: that one enters Umrah ihram upon Umrah ihram. Third: that one enters Umrah ihram upon Hajj ihram. Fourth: that one enters Hajj ihram upon Umrah ihram. He indicated the first with his statement: 'And whoever enters ihram for Hajj then enters another'; the second with his statement: 'And whoever completes his Umrah except for taqsir then enters another'; the third with his statement: 'And whoever enters ihram for Hajj then for Umrah then stands at Arafah'; and the fourth with his statement: 'A Makkan performed one shawt of tawaf for Umrah.' (Fath)
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the chapter on adding one ihram to another. The commentator explains that adding an ihram to another is a violation (jinaayah) for a Makkan and for those inside the miqat boundaries, but not for an aafaqi (one coming from outside the mawaaqeet), except in the specific case of adding the ihram of Umrah in the context of Hajj. The author places this chapter after the chapter on violations due to one consideration, and as a separate chapter due to another. The rulings are rationally divided into four categories, and the author's matn alludes to each. The first category is combining two Hajj ihrams; the second is combining two Umrah ihrams; the third is entering Umrah ihram after Hajj ihram; the fourth is entering Hajj ihram after Umrah ihram. The passage serves to orient the reader to the structure of the chapter.

Key Terms
إضافة الإحرام (idaafat al-ihraam): Adding one ihram to another, i.e., entering a second ihram while still in the first.
مكي (makki): A person whose residence is within the miqat boundaries of Makkah.
آفاقي (aafaqi): A person whose residence is outside the miqat boundaries.

Ruling on a Makkan Who Performs Tawaf for Umrah Then Enters Hajj
Intra-Hanafi dispute with agreement on boundary cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on which ihram a Makkan must refuse when combining Umrah and Hajj after partial tawaf, and explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When combining Umrah and Hajj, the weaker ihram is refused; dispute hinges on whether partial tawaf strengthens Umrah.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a Makkan who begins Umrah with a single shawt of tawaf and then enters Hajj. The question: which ihram must be refused (rafd)? Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ based on the strength of the Umrah ihram versus the ease of makeup. Understanding their arguments reveals how Hanafi usul principles like ta'akkud (strengthening) determine practical rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A Makkan performs at least one shawt of Umrah tawaf, then enters ihram for Hajj. Combining both is not legitimate for a Makkan, so one must be refused.
The minimum tawaf for Umrah is one shawt; the passage uses 'shawt' generically.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa rules that the Hajj must be refused. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule that the Umrah must be refused.
3
Analyze the proofs (talil)
Abu Hanifa argues that the Umrah ihram is strengthened (ta'akkud) by the partial tawaf, so the weaker unstrengthened Hajj ihram should be refused. The Sahibayn argue that Umrah is inferior, non-time-bound, and easier to make up, so it should be refused.
Both use the principle that the weaker ihram is more deserving of refusal, but they differ on which is weaker.
4
Note the agreed cases
If four or more shawts are performed, all agree to refuse Hajj. If no tawaf is performed before entering Hajj, all agree to refuse Umrah.
The degree of ta'akkud (strengthening) determines the consensus.
5
Determine the consequences
Refusing Hajj requires qada of both Hajj and Umrah and a dam. Refusing Umrah requires only qada of Umrah.
The dam is for performing tahlul before the proper time, based on the precedent of Aisha (RA).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مكي طاف شوطا لعمرة فأحرم بحج رفضه، وعليه حج وعمرة ودم لرفضه، أي بعد الإحرام للعمرة × قيد بالمكي؛ لأن الآفاقي لا يرفض واحداً منهما غير أنه إن أضاف الإحرام بعد فعل أقل الأشواط كان قارناً، وإلا فهو متمتع إن كان ذلك في أشهر الحج وقيد بالعمرة؛ لأنه لو أحرم بالحج وطاف له ثم بالعمرة، رفض العمرة اتفاقاً. . (فتح) شوطاً: المراد أقل أشواط العمرة، سواء كان واحدا أو اثنين أو ثلاثة. (ط) رفضه: [ أي عليه ترك الحج وجوبا بالتحلل منه بالحلق مثلا؛ تحاميا عن الإثم. (ط، مسكين)] الرفض: هو الترك، أي ترك الحج، وينبغي أن يكون الترك بالفعل بأن يحلق مثلا بعد الفراغ من أفعال العمرة ولا يكتفي بالقول أو النية، ووجه تركه أن الجمع بينهما في حق المكي غير مشروع، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا: يرفض العمرة؛ لأنها أدنى حالاً وأقل أعمالاً وأيسر قضاء؛ لكونها غير موقتة، وليس فيها إلا الطواف والسعي، وهي سنة، وليس الحج كذلك، ولأبي حنيفة: أن إحرام العمرة تأكد بما أتى به من الطواف وإحرام الحج لم يتأكد، وغير المتأكد أولى بالرفض؛ ولأن الرفض في العمرة نقضها وإبطالها، وفي الحج الامتناع عن الأداء، فهو أولى، ولو طاف للعمرة أربعة أشواط رفض الحج بلا خلاف، وكذا إذا أحرم بالعمرة ثم بالحج ولم يأت بشيء من العمرة يرفض العمرة بلا خلاف. (عيني، مستخلص) وعليه حج وعمرة: [ يتحلل بها؛ لأنه في معنى فائت الحج، حتى لو أتى به في سنته قضاء سقطت عنه العمرة. (ط)] لأنه كفائت الحج يتحلل بأفعال العمرة، ثم يأتي بالحج من قابل فعليه حج وعمرة، وقوله: "ودم لرفضه"، أي عليه دم لرفض الحج ؛ لأنه عليه أمر عائشة برفضها العمرة بالدم وهذا الدم بالتحلل قبل أوانه، ثم إن رفض العمرة قضاها فقط، وإن رفض الحج قضاه وقضى العمرة. (عيني، فتح)
A Makkan who performed one shawt of tawaf for Umrah then entered into ihram for Hajj refuses it (the Hajj), and upon him is (to perform) Hajj and Umrah and a dam for refusing it, i.e., after the ihram for Umrah. × It is restricted to the Makkan because the aafaqi does not refuse either of them, except that if he added the ihram after performing the minimum number of shawts, he becomes a qaarin; otherwise he is a mutamatti' if that was in the months of Hajj. And it is restricted to Umrah because if he entered ihram for Hajj and performed tawaf for it then for Umrah, he refuses the Umrah by agreement. (Fath) 'Shawt' means the minimum shawts of Umrah, whether one, two, or three. (T) 'Refuses it' means he must leave Hajj, by performing tahlul from it by shaving for example, to avoid sin. (T, Miskeen) Al-rafdh is leaving, i.e., leaving Hajj, and it should be by action such as shaving after completing the acts of Umrah, not merely by words or intention. The reason for leaving it is that combining both for a Makkan is not legitimate. This is according to Abu Hanifah. The two (Sahibayn) say: he refuses the Umrah because it is inferior, has fewer acts, and is easier to make up, as it is not time-bound and only involves tawaf and sa'y, and it is sunnah, whereas Hajj is not. According to Abu Hanifah, the ihram of Umrah is strengthened by the tawaf performed, while the ihram of Hajj is not strengthened, so the unstrengthened one is more deserving of refusal. Also, refusing Umrah is nullifying it, while refusing Hajj is merely refraining from performance, which is less severe. If he performed four shawts for Umrah, he refuses Hajj without disagreement. Similarly, if he entered ihram for Umrah then for Hajj and did not perform any act of Umrah, he refuses Umrah without disagreement. ('Ayni, Mustakhlas) 'And upon him is Hajj and Umrah' he makes tahlul with them because he is like one who missed Hajj; so even if he performs it as qada in the same year, the Umrah is dropped. (T) Because he is like one who missed Hajj, he makes tahlul with the acts of Umrah, then he comes with Hajj the following year, so upon him is Hajj and Umrah. And his statement 'and a dam for refusing it' means upon him is a dam for refusing the Hajj, because he was ordered, like Aisha, to refuse her Umrah with a dam, and this dam is for tahlul before its time. Then if he refused the Umrah, he only makes qada for it; if he refused the Hajj, he makes qada for it and also qada for the Umrah. ('Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a Makkan who performs one shawt of tawaf for Umrah and then enters into ihram for Hajj. The core issue is which of the two ihrams should be refused (rafd). According to Imam Abu Hanifah, the Hajj must be refused, because the Umrah ihram has been strengthened by the tawaf performed, making it more established, so the weaker (Hajj) is refused. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the Umrah should be refused, because it is lesser in status and easier to make up, as it is not time-bound and consists only of tawaf and sa'y. The passage then discusses agreed cases: if he performed four shawts, all agree he refuses Hajj; if he performed no tawaf at all, all agree he refuses Umrah. The consequence of refusing Hajj is that he must perform both Hajj and Umrah later and give a dam. The dam is for performing tahlul before the proper time. The explanation also distinguishes between refusal by action (shaving) and mere intention, emphasizing that actual tahlul is required. The commentator also notes the precedent of Aisha (RA) who was commanded to refuse her Umrah with a dam.

Key Terms
رفض (rafd): To abandon or refuse an ihram, requiring tahlul by action (e.g., shaving).
تأكد (ta'akkud): Strengthened; a legal concept where an act becomes more firmly established due to partial performance.
قضاء (qada'): Make-up or compensatory performance of an act that was missed or invalidated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a Makkan performed four shawts of Umrah tawaf and then entered Hajj, which ihram must be refused?
A) Hajj
B) Umrah
C) Both
D) None

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute, the choice of which ihram to refuse depends on whether the partial tawaf has strengthened the Umrah ihram (Abu Hanifa) or the ease of making up Umrah prevails (Sahibayn); the agreed boundary cases clarify the principle.

Ruling on a Makkan Proceeding with Both Ihrams
States the ruling if the Makkan does not refuse and performs both

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a Makkan performs both Hajj and Umrah in one journey and explain why the act is valid but requires a dam jabr.

Core Idea
A prohibited act can still be valid — prohibition does nullify validity in Hanafi fiqh.

We have learned that a Makkan is prohibited from performing both Hajj and Umrah separately in one journey. But what if he goes ahead and does both? This passage from al-Hidayah explains that the act is valid, but a penalty is required. The key Hanafi principle at work is that prohibition does not prevent the act's validity — an act can be valid and yet sinful. Let's unpack the reasoning and the unique nature of the required dam.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Identify the ruling: if he proceeds with both ihrams, the act is valid (sahih) but he owes one dam (penalty). This is the core legal outcome.
2
Understand the Principle
The commentator explains validity using the principle 'nahy ghayr man'' (prohibition does not prevent validity). The act can be valid despite being prohibited. Example: prayer in usurped land is valid but sinful.
This is a distinctive Hanafi usul principle.
3
Analyze the Penalty
Only one dam is required, not two, because the deficiency (nuqsan) occurs in only one of the two ihrams. The exact ihram is not specified; the single deficiency suffices.
The question of why not two dams is answered by the author.
4
Distinguish the Dam Type
This is a dam jabr (reparation) — a penalty for a deficiency. The offerer may not eat from its meat. This contrasts with the aafaqi's dam shukr (thanksgiving) which is permissible to eat.
Dam jabr: compensatory; dam shukr: optional joyful offering.
5
Apply the Principle
Recognize that this ruling is a direct application of the Hanafi position that nahy does not invalidate. This differs from other madhhabs who may hold that prohibition nullifies the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو مضى عليهما صح وعليه دمّ، صح الخ: لأنه أدى أفعالهما كما التزمهما إلا أنه منهي عنه، والنهي غير مانع لتحقق الفعل؛ لأن النهي يقرر المشروعية عندنا؛ لجواز أن يكون الشيء غير مشروع ويكون صحيحاً كالصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة، وقوله: "عليه دم" وجوب الدم لجمعه بينهما؛ لأنه يتمكن النقصان في عمله؛ لارتكاب النهي عنه، فإن قيل: لم لا يلزمه الدمان الحرمة كل واحد من الإحرامين؟ قلنا: لأنه غير ممنوع من أحدهما فالنقصان حيث ما كان تمكن في أحدهما، فلذلك لزمه دم واحد وهو دم جبر، لا يجوز له الأكل منه، بخلاف الآفاقي حيث يجوز له الأكل منه؛ لأن ذلك دم شكر في حقه. (عيني، مستخلص)
If he proceeds with both, it is valid and upon him is a dam. It is valid because he performed the acts of both as he obligated himself, except that it is prohibited. And prohibition does not prevent the realization of the act, because according to us (Hanafis), prohibition establishes legality (mashru'iyyah), as it is possible that a thing is not legitimate and yet is valid, like prayer in usurped land. And his statement 'upon him is a dam' means the obligation of a dam due to his combining both, because deficiency occurs in his action due to committing the prohibited. If it is asked: Why are two dams not required, one for the sanctity of each ihram? We say: Because he is not prohibited from one of them, so the deficiency is only in one of them. Therefore, one dam is required, and it is a dam of reparation (jabr), from which he may not eat, unlike the aafaqi, for whom it is a dam of thanksgiving and he may eat from it. ('Ayni, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when a Makkan does not refuse either ihram but goes ahead with both Hajj and Umrah. The ruling is that his ihram is valid (sahih) because he has performed the acts he obligated himself to do. However, since combining them was prohibited for him, he must offer a dam (penalty). The commentary provides the Hanafi principle: prohibition (nahy) does not invalidate the act; an act can be legally valid despite being prohibited (e.g., prayer in usurped land is valid but sinful). The dam is one, not two, because the deficiency only affects one of the two ihrams. This dam is a reparation (jabr) and the person may not eat from its meat, unlike the dam of an aafaqi who combines by becoming qaarin, which is a dam of thanksgiving and permissible to eat.

Key Terms
دم جبر (dam jabr): A compensatory dam resulting from a deficiency in the ritual; its meat may not be eaten by the offerer.
نهي غير مانع (nahy ghayr mani'): The principle that prohibition does not prevent the validity of the act itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Prohibition does not invalidate an act in Hanafi fiqh; a Makkan combining both ihrams must offer a single dam jabr from which he cannot eat.

Ruling on Entering a Second Hajj on the Day of Nahr
Clarifies the ruling when a person enters a second Hajj on the day of Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person enters a second Hajj on the day of Nahr, and identify when a dam is required.

Core Idea
Combining two Hajj ihrams is a bid'ah; the second is valid but requires a dam unless shaving was done first.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a rare but real scenario: a person already in ihram for Hajj enters a second Hajj on the day of Nahr. The ruling hinges on whether he has already shaved his head for the first Hajj. The text also involves an intra-Hanafi difference regarding a delay dam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering a second Hajj ihram while still in the first Hajj. The ruling is that the second Hajj becomes incumbent (lazim) – it is wajib to complete it.
This is based on the validity of starting the second ihram according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad al-Shaybani who invalidates it.
2
Apply the condition: shaving before the second ihram
If the pilgrim shaved (halq) or shortened (taqsir) for the first Hajj before entering the second, then the second Hajj is incumbent without any dam.
Shaving is an act of worship in the first Hajj, and it removes the conflict with the second ihram.
3
Contrast: no shaving before the second ihram
If the pilgrim has not shaved for the first Hajj and then enters the second, the second Hajj is still incumbent, but a dam (sacrifice) is required.
The dam is wajib because combining two Hajj ihrams is a bid'ah, and shaving the first before the second is out of its proper time, constituting a transgression against the second ihram.
4
Distinguish the two types of dam
The dam for combining (due to the bid'ah) is agreed upon by consensus among the Hanafi imams. Additionally, if he delays shaving the first Hajj beyond the days of Nahr, Abu Hanifa requires another dam for the delay; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say no dam for the delay.
This intra-Hanafi difference does not affect the rule that the second Hajj itself is valid and must be completed.
5
Apply the logic to a similar act (Umrah)
The text notes that the same ruling applies if someone combines two Umrah ihrams: it is a bid'ah and requires a dam. The principle is that entering a second 'umrah while in the first is similar to the Hajj case.
This extends the ruling to other combinations of the same type of pilgrimage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أحرم بحجّ ثم بآخر يوم النحر، فإن حلق في الأول لزمه الآخر، ولا دم، وإلا لزمه وعليه دم قصر أو لا، في الأول: أي الحج الأول قبل أن يحرم بالثاني ثم أحرم بالحج الثاني. (ط، ع) لزمه: أي الحج الآخر؛ لصحة الشروع فيه عندهما، خلافاً لمحمد. (ط) وإلا لزمه أي وإن لم يحلق للحج الأول وأحرم للثاني. [رمز الحقائق: ۱۸۳/۱] قصر أو لا : المراد بالتقصير الحلق؛ لأن التقصير لا دم فيه إنما فيه الصدقة؛ لأنه ارتفاق ناقص وعبر به؛ لتناول الذكر والأنثى، فذكر أولاً الحلق وثانياً التقصير؛ لما أن الأفضل في حق الرجل الحلق، وفي حقها التقصير، أي قصر بعد الفراغ من الأول قبل الفراغ من الثاني، أو لم يقصر بينهما وأخر حلق الأول إلى وقت الفراغ من الثاني، ووجوب الدم؛ لأن الجمع بين إحرامي الحج وإحرامي العمرة بدعة، فإذا حلق فهو وإن كان نسكاً في إحرام الحج الأول فهو جناية على إحرام الحج الثاني؛ لأنه في غير أوانه فيلزم الدم بالإجماع، وإن لم يحلق حتى حج في العام القابل فقد أخر الحلق عن وقته في إحرام الأول، وذلك يوجب الدم عند أبي حنيفة للتأخير، وعندهما لا يلزمه شيء بتأخير الحلق عن وقته وهو أيام النحر. (عيني، مستخلص)
And whoever enters into ihram for Hajj then for another Hajj on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), if he shaved his head in the first, the other becomes incumbent upon him and there is no dam; otherwise, it becomes incumbent upon him and upon him is a dam, whether he shortens (his hair) or not. Commentary: 'In the first' means the first Hajj before he enters the second, then he entered the second. (T, 'Ayn) 'It becomes incumbent' means the other Hajj becomes incumbent, due to the validity of starting it according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad. (T) 'Otherwise it becomes incumbent' means if he did not shave for the first Hajj and entered the second. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/183] 'Shortens or not' means the intended meaning of taqsir is shaving; because taqsir does not require a dam, only sadaqah, because it is an incomplete benefit; he used it to include both males and females. So he mentioned shaving first then taqsir because for men shaving is preferable, for women taqsir. That is, he shortened after finishing the first before finishing the second, or he did not shorten between them and delayed shaving the first until the time of finishing the second. The obligation of the dam is because combining two Hajj ihrams or two Umrah ihrams is a bid'ah. So if he shaved, although it is a nusk in the first Hajj ihram, it is a transgression against the second Hajj ihram because it is out of its proper time, so a dam is required by consensus. And if he did not shave until he performed Hajj the following year, he has delayed the shave from its time in the first ihram, and that requires a dam according to Abu Hanifah due to the delay; according to the two (Sahibayn), nothing is required from delaying the shave beyond its time, which is the days of Nahr. ('Ayni, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage deals with a person who performs a second Hajj on the day of Nahr while still in the first Hajj. The ruling depends on whether he has already shaved his head (halq) for the first Hajj. If he shaved before entering the second ihram, the second Hajj becomes incumbent (lazim) and no dam is required. If he did not shave, the second Hajj is still incumbent but he must give a dam. The commentary explains that 'shaving' here includes taqsir (shortening) as well. There is a secondary difference: according to Abu Hanifah, if he delays shaving beyond the days of Nahr, he must also give a dam for the delay; the Sahibayn say no dam for delay. The dam for combining is by consensus, but the dam for delay is only according to Abu Hanifah. The reason for the dam is that combining two Hajj ihrams or two Umrah ihrams is a bid'ah (innovation). Shaving for the first Hajj during the days of Nahr is an act of worship, but if it delays the second Hajj's start, it becomes a violation.

Key Terms
لزمه (lazimahu): It becomes incumbent/lazim upon him; here meaning the second Hajj is valid and must be completed.
بدعة (bid'ah): Innovation in religion; combining two Hajj or Umrah ihrams is considered a bid'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if a person enters a second Hajj on the day of Nahr without having shaved for the first?
A) The second Hajj is invalid
B) The second Hajj is incumbent and he owes a dam
C) He must only perform the first Hajj
D) He must perform both without any dam

Key Takeaway
Entering a second Hajj on the day of Nahr is valid and obligatory to complete, but requires a dam if not preceded by shaving or shortening for the first Hajj.

Ruling on Entering a Second Umrah After Taqsir
States the obligation of a dam for combining two Umrahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for combining two Umrahs and explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding two Hajjs.

Core Idea
Combining two Umrahs before taqsir requires a dam; the act is makruh tahrimi.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hajj/Umrah: a person who completes all Umrah acts except hair shortening (taqsir) and then enters a second Umrah. The classical Hanafi text rules that a dam (sacrificial animal) becomes wajib. The commentary explores the rationale and highlights an internal difference over whether the same applies to two Hajjs in one year.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine the exact situation: the person has done all Umrah acts except taqsir, then puts on a new ihram for another Umrah before taqsir of the first.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that a dam becomes wajib. The act of combining two Umrahs in this manner is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The dam is a compensation for the prohibited combination.
3
Note the distinction between Umrah and Hajj
The author (Kanz) distinguishes this case from combining two Hajjs: here a dam is wajib for Umrah, but not for Hajj according to al-Jami' al-Saghir. In al-Asl, a dam is wajib for both.
This shows an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Understand al-Zayla'i's rationale
Al-Zayla'i explains that the prohibition arises from deficiency in the acts. For two Umrahs, both occur at the same time, causing deficiency. For two Hajjs, the second's acts are deferred to the next year, so no deficiency at the time of ihram.
This difference explains why some riwayaat do not require a dam for two Hajjs.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The more common position in the madhhab is to require a dam for combining two Hajj ihrams as well, but the text leaves it as a riwayah difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن فرغ من عمرته إلا التقصير فأحرم بأخرى لزمه دم، لزمه دم: لأنه جمع بين إحرامي العمرة، ثم إن المصنف فرق بين الحج والعمرة كما ترى، وأوجب في العمرة دماً ولم يوجب في الحج، وهو رواية "الجامع الصغير"، وفي "الأصل": أوجب الدم في الحج أيضاً؛ للجمع بينهما إحراماً، ولا فرق بين الجمعين رمز الحقائق: ۱۸۳/۱] وقال الزيلعي: الفرق أن الجمع في الإحرام إنما كان حراما لأجل الجمع في الأفعال؛ إذ الجمع يوجب نقصاً، وهذا القدر ثابت في العمرتين مفقود في الحجين؛ لأن أفعال الثانية تتأخر إلى القابل، وفيه إفادة أن الجمع بين العمرتين حرام، أي مكروه تحريماً، وفي "الهداية": إنه بدعة. (فتح)
And whoever completes his Umrah except for taqsir (shortening of hair), then enters into another Umrah, a dam is incumbent upon him. Commentary: A dam is incumbent because he combined two Umrah ihrams. Then the author (Kanz) distinguished between Hajj and Umrah, as you see, and made a dam wajib in Umrah but not in Hajj. This is the riwayah of al-Jami' al-Saghir. In al-Asl, he made a dam wajib for Hajj as well, due to combining them in ihram, and there is no difference between the two combinations. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/183] Al-Zayla'i said: The difference is that combining in ihram is prohibited only due to combining in acts, because combining causes deficiency. This deficiency is present in two Umrahs but absent in two Hajjs, because the acts of the second are deferred to the following year. This indicates that combining two Umrahs is haram, i.e., makruh tahrimi, and in al-Hidayah it is called a bid'ah. (Fath)
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage covers the case of a person who has performed all acts of Umrah except the final taqsir (hair shortening) and then enters a second Umrah. The ruling is that he must give a dam because he has combined two Umrah ihrams, which is prohibited. The commentary notes a difference between the author's ruling here and the previous case of two Hajjs: in the current text, a dam is required for Umrah but not for Hajj (as per al-Jami' al-Saghir), but in al-Asl, a dam is required for both. Al-Zayla'i explains the reason: the prohibition and deficiency from combining acts is present when the acts of both occur in the same time, as with two Umrahs. With two Hajjs, the second's acts are postponed to the next year, so no deficiency occurs at the time of the second ihram. The passage also establishes that combining two Umrahs is makruh tahrimi (haram) or bid'ah.

Key Terms
تقصير (taqsir): Shortening the hair, the final act of Umrah or Hajj; here it is the only incomplete act before entering the second Umrah.
جمع بين العمرتين (jam' bayna al-umratayn): Combining two Umrahs by entering a second after completing all but taqsir of the first.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because Umrah is sunnah, Hajj is fard
B) Because the acts of the second Umrah occur immediately, causing deficiency, while the second Hajj's acts are delayed
C) Because the author made a mistake
D) Because the Sahibayn say so

Key Takeaway
Combining two Umrahs before taqsir of the first is makruh tahrimi and requires a dam; the same for two Hajjs is disputed within the school.

Combining Two Hajj or Two Umrah Ihrams
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity and penalty for combining two Hajj or two Umrah ihrams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining two Hajj or two Umrah ihrams, explain why it is valid but requires a dam, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of a dam for two Hajj.

Core Idea
Combining two ihrams of the same type is valid but requires a dam; the Hanafi school has internal differences on when the dam is due.

What happens if someone enters ihram for Hajj, then on the Day of Nahr enters another Hajj ihram? Or performs two Umrahs in one trip? The Hanafi school holds the actions are valid, but a penalty animal (dam) is required. However, there is a dispute within the school on whether a dam applies to two Hajj as well, and on delaying the shaving ritual. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is combining two ihrams of the same type (Hajj-Hajj or Umrah-Umrah). The ruling: the actions are valid (sahih) but the combination is a bid'ah (innovation) and makruh tahriman.
The text states 'صح' (valid) but requires a dam.
2
Distinguish between Hajj and Umrah cases
For Umrah, a dam is always required when combining two Umrahs. For Hajj, the ruling depends on the narration: in al-Jami' al-Saghir no dam is required, but in al-Asl a dam is required. The relied-upon position is the former.
Al-Zayla'i explains the difference: the actions of the second Hajj are delayed to the next year, so no deficiency occurs.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on delaying halq
If one delays shaving (halq) from its time (Days of Nahr) to the next year, Abu Hanifa holds a dam is required; the Sahibayn hold nothing is due.
The dispute is on whether the time for halq is expansive (Sahibayn) or fixed (Abu Hanifa).
4
Apply the usul principle: nahy does not invalidate
The combination is prohibited (nahy), but the prohibition does not nullify the act. Analogous to prayer in usurped land: the act is valid but sinful.
This is established in Hanafi usul an-nahy does not indicate fasād unless it pertains to the essence of the act.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that combining two Umrahs requires a dam; combining two Hajj does not require a dam. This is from al-Jami' al-Saghir and preferred by later scholars like al-Zayla'i.
This distinction is based on the feasibility of completing actions without deficiency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج إضافة الإحرام إلى الإحرام فلو مضى عليهما صح وعليه دمّ، ومن أحرم بحجّ ثم بآخر يوم النحر، فإن حلق في أي أتمهما المكي أي أحرم نحج آخر الأول لزمه الآخر، ولا دم، وإلا لزمه وعليه دم قصر أو لا، ومن فرغ من عمرته إلا التقصير فأحرم بأخرى لزمه دم، أي بعمرة أخرى للجمع بين العمرتين صح الخ: لأنه أدى أفعالهما كما التزمهما إلا أنه منهي عنه، والنهي غير مانع لتحقق الفعل؛ لأن النهي يقرر المشروعية عندنا؛ لجواز أن يكون الشيء غير مشروع ويكون صحيحاً كالصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة، وقوله: "عليه دم" وجوب الدم لجمعه بينهما؛ لأنه يتمكن النقصان في عمله؛ لارتكاب النهي عنه، فإن قيل: لم لا يلزمه الدمان الحرمة كل واحد من الإحرامين؟ قلنا: لأنه غير ممنوع من أحدهما فالنقصان حيث ما كان تمكن في أحدهما، فلذلك لزمه دم واحد وهو دم جبر، لا يجوز له الأكل منه، بخلاف الآفاقي حيث يجوز له الأكل منه؛ لأن ذلك دم شكر في حقه. (عيني، مستخلص) في الأول: أي الحج الأول قبل أن يحرم بالثاني ثم أحرم بالحج الثاني. (ط، ع) لزمه: أي الحج الآخر؛ لصحة الشروع فيه عندهما، خلافاً لمحمد. (ط) وإلا لزمه أي وإن لم يحلق للحج الأول وأحرم للثاني. [رمز الحقائق: ۱۸۳/۱] قصر أو لا : المراد بالتقصير الحلق؛ لأن التقصير لا دم فيه إنما فيه الصدقة؛ لأنه ارتفاق ناقص وعبر به؛ لتناول الذكر والأنثى، فذكر أولاً الحلق وثانياً التقصير؛ لما أن الأفضل في حق الرجل الحلق، وفي حقها التقصير، أي قصر بعد الفراغ من الأول قبل الفراغ من الثاني، أو لم يقصر بينهما وأخر حلق الأول إلى وقت الفراغ من الثاني، ووجوب الدم؛ لأن الجمع بين إحرامي الحج وإحرامي العمرة بدعة، فإذا حلق فهو وإن كان نسكاً في إحرام الحج الأول فهو جناية على إحرام الحج الثاني؛ لأنه في غير أوانه فيلزم الدم بالإجماع، وإن لم يحلق حتى حج في العام القابل فقد أخر الحلق عن وقته في إحرام الأول، وذلك يوجب الدم عند أبي حنيفة للتأخير، وعندهما لا يلزمه شيء بتأخير الحلق عن وقته وهو أيام النحر. (عيني، مستخلص) عمرته أي من أفعالها التي شرع فيها ولم يبق عليه. (ع) لزمه دم: لأنه جمع بين إحرامي العمرة، ثم إن المصنف فرق بين الحج والعمرة كما ترى، وأوجب في العمرة دماً ولم يوجب في الحج، وهو رواية "الجامع الصغير"، وفي "الأصل": أوجب الدم في الحج أيضاً؛ للجمع بينهما إحراماً، ولا فرق بين الجمعين [رمز الحقائق: ۱۸۳/۱] وقال الزيلعي: الفرق أن الجمع في الإحرام إنما كان حراما لأجل الجمع في الأفعال؛ إذ الجمع يوجب نقصاً، وهذا القدر ثابت في العمرتين مفقود في الحجين؛ لأن أفعال الثانية تتأخر إلى القابل، وفيه إفادة أن الجمع بين العمرتين حرام، أي مكروه تحريماً، وفي "الهداية": إنه بدعة. (فتح)
The Book of Hajj: Adding Ihram to Ihram. If two (ihrams) pass (i.e., one performs both), it is valid and he owes a dam. Whoever enters ihram for Hajj then another on the day of Nahr, if he shaves in whichever of the two he completes – the Makki? – the first necessitates the other, and no dam, otherwise it necessitates and he owes a dam, whether he shortens or not. Whoever finishes his Umrah except the taqsir and enters ihram for another, he owes a dam. ... (commentary) ... Al-Zayla'i said: The difference is that combining in ihram is prohibited only because of combining in actions; since combining causes deficiency, this is present in two Umrahs but absent in two Hajj because the actions of the second are delayed to the next year. This shows that combining two Umrahs is haram, i.e., makruh tahriman, and in al-Hidaya: it is a bid'ah.
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on combining two ihrams of the same type (Hajj-Hajj or Umrah-Umrah). The matn states that if one performs two Hajj or two Umrah ihrams, the actions are valid (sahih) but a dam (penalty sacrificial animal) is required. The commentary explains that the prohibition does not invalidate the act because, according to the Hanafi principle, the prohibition confirms the act's legislated nature while allowing validity despite prohibition, analogous to prayer in usurped land. For two Hajj ihrams: if one enters ihram for Hajj then another on the day of Nahr, and shaves for the first, the second becomes binding and no dam is due; if he does not shave until after completing the second, he owes a dam whether he shaves after finishing or delays. For delaying the shaving beyond the days of Nahr until the next year, Abu Hanifa holds that a dam is required for the delay, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold nothing is due. For two Umrahs: if one completes an Umrah except the taqsir (hair shortening) and then enters ihram for another, he owes a dam. The commentary notes a difference in narration: in al-Jami' al-Saghir, dam is only for two Umrahs, while in al-Asl, dam is also for two Hajj. Al-Zayla'i explains the distinction: combining two Umrahs involves deficiency in actions because both are performed in the same year, whereas two Hajj are separated by a year, so no deficiency. The combination is considered a bid'ah (innovation) and is makruh tahriman.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A penalty sacrificial animal required for certain violations during Hajj/Umrah, such as combining two ihrams or delaying rituals.
بدعة (bid'ah): An innovation in religious practice; here, combining two ihrams of the same type is considered a bid'ah and is makruh tahriman.
حلق (halq): Shaving the head, a ritual of exiting ihram; in this context, its timing is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (al-Jami' al-Saghir), what is the ruling for combining two Hajj ihrams?
A) It is invalid and requires a dam.
B) It is valid and requires a dam.
C) It is valid and does not require a dam.
D) It is invalid and requires no dam.

Key Takeaway
Combining two Hajj or two Umrah ihrams is valid but considered a bid'ah; a dam is required for two Umrahs but not for two Hajj according to the relied-upon narration.

Combining Hajj and Umrah Ihrams: Three Scenarios
Rulings for combining Hajj and Umrah ihrams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for combining Hajj and Umrah ihrams and apply the appropriate ruling for each.

Core Idea
A combined Hajj-Umrah ihram is valid but may require rafd and a dam if the order is disrupted.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq details the rulings when a pilgrim combines intentions for Hajj and Umrah. The rulings depend on the timing and sequence of actions. Understanding these scenarios prevents invalid or sinful acts during the sacred journey.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the matn and commentary to find the three distinct cases: (1) ihram for Hajj then Umrah before standing at Arafat; (2) performing tawaf for Hajj then ihram for Umrah and doing both; (3) ihram for Umrah during the days of Tashreeq after Hajj pillars.
Each scenario has a different ruling regarding rafd and dam.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For scenario (1): automatic rafd of Umrah upon standing at Arafat. For (2): dam is required and it is recommended to abandon the Umrah. For (3): Umrah is valid but makruh tahriman, must be abandoned, requiring dam and qada.
The passage uses the term 'rafd' for abandonment.
3
Understand the reasoning
The commentary explains that standing at Arafat makes Umrah actions impossible (1). In (2), the Hajj is affirmed by tawaf al-qudum, so combining is worse and requires expiation. In (3), Umrah during Tashreeq is disliked to glorify Hajj, so it must be abandoned.
The analogy with fasting on the day of Nahr clarifies why qada is required for Umrah but not for fasting.
4
Apply the qiyas with fasting on the day of Nahr
Compare: starting a forbidden fast requires breaking it but no qada because the sin is immediate; starting Umrah during Tashreeq is valid but the sin is in the actions, so qada is required after rafd. This distinction is based on the nature of the prohibited act.
This deepens understanding of the ruling's rationale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عرفات ومن أحرم بحج ثم بعمرة ثم وقف بعرفات فقد رفض عمرته، وإن توجّه إليها لا، بالوقوف أي صار تاركا للعمرة فلو طاف للحج ثم أحرم بعمرة ومضى عليهما يجب دمّ وندب رفضها، وإن أهل بعمرة لكنه يصير أي طواف القدوم حتى أي استحب أي أحرم ثم بعمرة: [ أي أحرم بها قبل إتمام الحج وأراد الجمع بينهما. (ط،ع)] صورته: آفاقي أحرم بحجة ثم بعمرة قبل الإتيان بشيء من أفعال الحج؛ لأن الجمع بينهما مشروع في حقه؛ لأنه يمكنه إتيان أفعال العمرة قبل أفعال الحج، لكنه أخطأ السنة؛ لترك الترتيب، أو المقارنة في الإحرام، فيصير مسيئاً، وقوله: "فقد رفض عمرته"؛ لأنه تعذر عليه أداؤها بعد الوقوف؛ إذ هي مبنية على الحج وهو غير مشروع، وإذا توجه إلى عرفة لا يرفض العمرة؛ لأنه غير مأمور بنقض العمرة فاشترط أقصى ما يكون وهو الوقوف بخلاف مصلي الظهر حيث تبطل بالسعي إلى الجمعة؛ لأنه مأمور بنقض الظهر، فاكتفي بأدنى ما يكون من خصائص الجمعة، وهو السعي. (مستخلص، فتح) بعرفات: قبل أن يدخل مكة وقبل أن يأتي بأفعال العمرة. (ط،ع) لا: أي لا تاركاً للعمرة يقف بها. (ط، ع) فلو طاف أي الرجل الذي أراد الجمع بين الحج والعمرة. (عيني) ومضى عليهما بأن قدم أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج. وقوله : يجب" دم؛ للجمع بينهما؛ لأنه قارن، مسيء به أكثر من الأول؛ لأن الإساءة في الأول بتقديم إحرام الحج على العمرة، وههنا به وبتقديم بعض أفعال الحج، وإليه أشار بقوله : فلو طاف للحج"، أي للتحية، وهذا دم كفارة لا دم نسك، وهو الصحيح. ندب رفضها: [أي ترك العمرة في هذه الصورة؛ لأن الحج قد تأكد ببعض أفعاله، وإذا رفض العمرة قضاها؛ لصحة المشروع فيها، وعليه دم لرفضها. (ط، ع)] أي العمرة، يدل على أنه دم شكر، فإنه لم يين أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج؛ لأن ما أتى به إنما هو سنة، فيمكنه بناء أفعال الحج على أفعال العمرة، فلا موجب للجبر، ولأن طواف القدوم ليس من سنن نفس الحج، بل هو سنة قدوم المسجد الحرام كركعتي التحية لغيره من ا ولهذا يسقط بطواف آخر من مشروعات الوقت، واستحباب رفض العمرة؛ لأنه فات الترتيب في الفعل من وجه؛ لتقديم طواف القدوم، وفيما سبق لم يفت؛ لأنه هناك لم يقدم إلا الإحرام ولا ترتيب فيه، ولا يلزمه الرفض هنا؛ لأن المؤدى ليس بركن الحج وإذا رفضها قضاها لصحة الشروع فيها، وعليه دم لرفضها. (فتح) أهل بعمرة: لزوم الرفض تخلصاً عن الإثم لا يخص يوم النحر بل في أيام التشريق أيضاً، وقوله: "لزمته" لصحة الشروع فيها، لكن مع كراهة التحريم، ولزمه رفض العمرة تخلصاً من الإثم؛ لأنه أدى أركان الحج فكان بانياً أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج من كل وجه، فكان خطأ محضاً، وقد كرهت العمرة في هذه الأيام تعظيماً لأمر الحج فترفض العمرة، وإذا رفض العمرة يجب الدم لرفضها؛ للتحلل منها قبل أوانه، ويجب القضاء أيضاً؛ لصحة الشروع فيها، بخلاف صوم يوم النحر ؛ فإنه إذا أفسده بعد ما شرع فيه لا يلزمه قضاؤه؛ لأنه بنفس الشروع قد باشر المنهي، فيجب عليه إفساده، ولا يجب عليه صيانته، ووجوب القضاء فرع وجوب الصيانة، وههنا بنفس الشروع لم يباشر المنهي، وهو أفعال العمرة، فصار كالصلاة في الأرض المغصوبة. (فتح)
Arafat. Whoever enters ihram for Hajj then for Umrah then stands at Arafat has abandoned his Umrah, but if he heads towards it (Arafat) without standing, no. By standing, i.e., he becomes a leaver of the Umrah. So if he performs tawaf for Hajj then enters ihram for Umrah and passes (performs) both, a dam is required and it is recommended to abandon the Umrah. And if one pronounces talbiyah for Umrah... (commentary) ... The abandonment of Umrah to escape sin is not specific to the day of Nahr but also applies to the days of Tashreeq. His saying: 'it becomes binding' for the validity of the commencement, but with karahah tahrim. He must abandon the Umrah to escape sin, because he performed the pillars of Hajj, so he was building the actions of Umrah upon the actions of Hajj completely, which is pure error. Umrah is disliked in these days to glorify Hajj, so he abandons the Umrah. If he abandons it, dam is required for leaving it before its time, and qada' is also required due to valid commencement, unlike fasting on the day of Nahr, where if he invalidates it after starting, no qada' is required because by the commencement he already committed the prohibited act. Here, by commencement he did not commit the prohibited act, which is the actions of Umrah, so it is like prayer in usurped land.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on combining a Hajj ihram with an Umrah ihram in the same journey. The matn presents three scenarios: (1) If one enters ihram for Hajj then for Umrah and then stands at Arafat before performing any Umrah actions, his Umrah is considered abandoned (rafd). If he only heads towards Arafat without standing, the Umrah remains intact. (2) If one performs tawaf for Hajj (tawaf al-qudum) and then enters ihram for Umrah and proceeds with both, a dam is required and it is recommended (mustahab) to abandon the Umrah. (3) If one enters ihram for Umrah during the days of Tashreeq (after Hajj), the Umrah is binding but with karahah tahrim (disliked to the level of prohibition), and he must abandon it to avoid sin; upon abandonment, he owes a dam and must make it up (qada'). The commentary explains the reasoning: For scenario (1), standing at Arafat makes it impossible to perform the Umrah because its actions must precede Hajj, so it is automatically abandoned. For scenario (2), since the pilgrim has already performed part of Hajj (tawaf al-qudum), the Hajj is affirmed, and to combine properly, it is better to drop the Umrah; the dam here is a kaffarah (expiation) not a nusk (thanksgiving) because the error is greater. For scenario (3), the Umrah is valid but makruh because performing Umrah during the days of Tashreeq diminishes the honor of Hajj; it must be abandoned to avoid the sin, requiring dam and qada. The commentary compares this to fasting on the day of Nahr: if one starts a forbidden fast, he is required to break it and no qada is due because the sin is immediate; but for Umrah, the sin is in the actions, not the mere ihram, so qada is required.

Key Terms
رفض (rafd): Abandonment of a validly commenced Umrah to correct the combination with Hajj.
دم كفارة (dam kaffarah): A sacrificial animal as expiation for a more severe violation, from which the pilgrim may not eat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In scenario (2), what is the status of the dam required?
A) It is a dam nusk (thanksgiving) from which the pilgrim may eat.
B) It is a dam kaffarah (expiation) from which the pilgrim may not eat.
C) It is not required if the pilgrim abandons the Umrah.
D) It is only required if the pilgrim completes both Hajj and Umrah.

Key Takeaway
Combining Hajj and Umrah ihrams is valid but requires careful observance of timing; disruption of order may necessitate dam and abandonment of one ihram.

Ruling on Combining Hajj and Umrah Before Standing at Arafat
Ruling on combining Hajj and Umrah ihram before standing at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a person enters ihram for Hajj then for Umrah and then stands at Arafat, and explain why the Umrah is considered abandoned.

Core Idea
If you stand at Arafat after combining Hajj and Umrah ihram, your Umrah is automatically abandoned — Umrah acts are no longer feasible.

This lesson examines the first scenario from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: a person who enters ihram for Hajj, then for Umrah, and then goes to Arafat. The text rules that his Umrah is abandoned. We will understand the condition that triggers this ruling and the reasoning behind it, including an analogy with Friday prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering ihram for Hajj, then for Umrah, then standing at Arafat. The ruling is that the Umrah is considered abandoned (rafd al-umrah).
The abandonment occurs automatically upon standing at Arafat.
2
Understand the condition
The text specifies that abandonment only occurs if he actually stands at Arafat. If he merely heads towards Arafat (tawajjaha ilayha) without standing, he is not considered to have abandoned the Umrah.
3
Explore the reasoning
After standing at Arafat, performing Umrah is impossible because Umrah must be performed before the Hajj acts. Standing at Arafat is a key Hajj ritual that marks the start of Hajj proper, making Umrah unfeasible in the correct order.
The Hanafi position is that the order of Hajj and Umrah cannot be reversed; once Hajj acts begin, Umrah cannot be interjected.
4
Compare with the Friday prayer analogy
The text analogizes to a person praying Zuhr who must abandon it upon hearing the call to Friday prayer. The difference is that in the Hajj case, the person is not commanded to abandon the Umrah unless he actually stands at Arafat, whereas in prayer, the mere call suffices because the person is obligated to abandon Zuhr explicitly.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that one is not required to abandon an act unless another act becomes obligatory and incompatible.

Book of Hajj
Addition of Ihram to Ihram
Arafat
Whoever enters ihram for Hajj then for Umrah then stands at Arafat has abandoned his Umrah; and if he goes to it (Arafat) not (abandoning) – by standing means he becomes a deserter of Umrah. So if he performed tawaf for Hajj then entered ihram for Umrah and proceeded with both, a blood sacrifice is obligatory and it is recommended to abandon it (the Umrah). And if he entered ihram for Umrah...
[Detailed explanation follows on various scenarios]
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, Book of Hajj, discusses the rulings for someone who combines the ihram of Hajj and Umrah. The author presents several scenarios: (1) If one enters ihram for Hajj, then for Umrah before any Hajj acts, then stands at Arafat – his Umrah is considered abandoned because after standing at Arafat, performing Umrah is not feasible (as Umrah is built upon Hajj in a certain order). (2) If he goes to Arafat without having entered Makkah or performed Umrah acts, he is not considered having abandoned Umrah. (3) If he performed tawaf for Hajj (either greeting tawaf or obligatory) then entered ihram for Umrah and continued with both, a dam (blood sacrifice) is obligatory as qarin (one performing Qiran) and it is recommended to abandon the Umrah. The commentary explains that the dam is expiatory (kaffarah) not a ritual sacrifice (dam nusuk). The reason for recommending abandonment is that Hajj has become confirmed by some of its actions, and if he abandons Umrah, he must make it up later with another dam. (4) If one enters ihram for Umrah on the Day of Nahr or during Tashriq days, it is valid but makruh tahriman, and he must abandon it, give dam, and make up the Umrah. The passage draws an analogy to the Friday prayer situation where a person praying Zuhr is ordered to abandon it upon hearing the call to Friday prayer. It distinguishes between cases where the prohibition is immediate versus when it is not, affecting the obligation to make up the act.

Key Terms
رفض العمرة (rafḍ al-ʿumrah): Abandoning the Umrah after having entered ihram for it, due to conflict with Hajj obligations.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (sheep or goat) required as expiation for certain violations during Hajj/Umrah.
قارن (qārin): One who performs Qiran, i.e., combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram or separate ihrams with certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Kanz al-Daqa'iq, what is the ruling on the Umrah of a person who enters ihram for Hajj, then for Umrah, and then stands at Arafat?
A) The Umrah is valid and he becomes a qarin.
B) The Umrah is abandoned and must be made up later.
C) The Umrah is invalid without any penalty.
D) The Umrah is merged into the Hajj.

Key Takeaway
If you stand at Arafat after combining Hajj and Umrah ihram in the wrong order, your Umrah is automatically abandoned and must be made up later.
