كتاب الحج الحج عن الغير فقط، والشرط العجز الدائم إلى وقت الموت، وإنما شرط عجز المنوب للحج أي لا تجزئ عند القدرة في المنوب الفرض لا النفل ومن أحرم. من مع ليس له ذلك، ولا يصل إلى الميت؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَنْ لَيْسَ لِلْإِنْسَانِ إِلَّا مَا سَعَى (النجم: ۳۹)، وقال مالك والشافعي: يجوز ذلك في الصدقة والعبادة المالية والحج ولا يجوز في غيره من الطاعات كالصلاة والصوم وقراءة القرآن وغيره، ولنا: ما روي أن رجلا سأل النبي له فقال : "يا رسول الله ! كان لي أبوان أبرهما حال حياتهما فكيف لي برهما بعد موتهما؟ فقال النبي "إن البر أن تصلي لهما لهما صلاتك، وأن تصوم مع صيامك"، رواه الدار قطني، أي تجعل لهما ثواب صلاتك وصومك، وما رواه معقل بن يسار له أنه قال: قال رسول الله : "اقرءوا على موتاكم سورة يس"، رواه أبو داود. وما روي أنه عليه ضحى بكبشين أملحين أحدهما عن نفسه والآخر عن أمته، متفق عليه أي جعل ثوابه لأمته، وما روى أنس له أنه سأل النبي الله فقال : يا رسول الله ! إنا نتصدق عن موتانا ونحج عنهم وندعو لهم فهل يصل إليهم ذلك؟ قال: "نعم! إنه ليصل إليهم ويفرحون به كما يفرح أحدكم بالطبق إذا أهدي إليه"، رواه أبو جعفر العكبرى، والآية منسوخة بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَاتَّبَعَتْهُمْ ذُرِّيَّتُهُمْ بِإيمان ألحقنا بهم ذريتهم الله، فأدخل الأبناء بصلاح الآباء، قال بنسخها ابن عباس، وقيل: هي خاصة بقوم موسى وإبراهيم الاملا لأنه وقع حكاية عما في صحفهما بقوله: ﴿أَمْ لَمْ يُنَبَّاً بِمَا فِي صُحُفِ مُوسَى وَإِبْرَاهِيمَ الَّذِي وَفَى (النجم: ٣٦ ٣٧)، وقيل: أريد بالإنسان الكافر، وأما المؤمن فله ما سعى أخوه، وقيل: ليس له من طريق العدل وله من طريق الفضل، وقيل: اللام بمعنى "على" كما في قوله: ﴿وَلَهُمُ اللَّعْنَةُ (غافر: ٥٢)، وقوله: ﴿وَإِنْ أَسَأْتُمْ فَلَهَا ﴾ (الإسراء: (٧) [رمز الحقائق: ١٨٦/١] (فتح) نفسه فقط : أي شرط جواز الإنابة في الحج (ع) إلى وقت الموت [كالزمانة وقطع الرجلين، وإن أحج عن وهو مريض أو محبوس، فإن مات جاز وإن زال العذر بطل. (ط)] إن كان الحج فرضاً بأن وجب عليه، وهو قادر ثم عجز بعد ذلك، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يجب الإحجاج على العاجز إن كان له مال، فلا يشترط أن يجب عليه وهو صحيح، فلو أحج غيره ثم عجز لا يجزئه و به صرح غير واحد، ومن هنا يؤخذ عدم صحة ما يفعله السلاطين والوزراء من الاستنابة عن أنفسهم في الحج؛ لأن عجزهم ليس مستمرا إلى الموت، وإنما شرط دوام العجز؛ لأنه فرض العمر حتى لو أحج عن نفسه وهو مريض يكون موقوفا، فإن مات أجزأه، وإن صح بطل، فعليه حجة الإسلام والمؤدى تطوع، وكذا لو أحج . نفسه عن وهو محبوس. (عيني، فتح) المنوب: بضم الميم وفتح النون وكسر الواو المشددة من التنويب بمعنى المنيب. لا النفل: [لأن باب النفل أوسع فيجوز للصحيح المستطيع إحجاج رجل بماله تطوعا. (مسكين (ط) ] لأن في حج النفل تجوز الإنابة مع القدرة؛ لأن باب النفل أوسع؛ ألا ترى أنه يجوز النفل في الصلاة قاعداً أو راكباً مع القدرة على القيام والنزول، والصحيح من المذهب في من عن غيره أن أصل الحج يقع عن المحجوج عنه؛ لحديث الخثعمية قالت: "يا رسول الله ! إن فريضة الله في الحج أدركت أبي شيخاً كبيراً لا يثبت على الراحلة أفأحج عنه؟" قال: "نعم"، متفق عليه، وعن محمد أن الحج يقع عن الحاج وللآمر ثواب النفقة، ولا يسقط فرض الحج عن النائب، بل يكون نقلاً؛ لأنه لا يتأدى إلا بنية الفرض أو مطلق النية و لم توجد وإنما وجدت النية عن الآمر. (فتح عيني) آمريه بأن أمره رجلان أن يحج عن كل منهما فأحرم عنهما فالحج له. [رمز الحقائق: ۱۸۷/۱] ضمن النفقة: الأنه خالفهما ولا يقع الحج عنهما بل يقع عن نفسه. (ط، ع)] لآمريه، وفيه إيماء إلى أنها لا تقع عن أحدهما؛ لأن كل واحد إنما أمره أن يخلص النية له ولا يمكنه الإيقاع عن أحدهما؛ لعدم الأولوية، فوقعت عن المأمور وإن نوى أحدهما غير عين فإن مضى على ذلك صار مخالفا بالاتفاق، وإن عين أحدهما قبل الطواف والوقوف عن نقلاً، عنه جاز عند الطرفين ويقع عنه، ويضمن النفقة للثاني، وعند أبي يوسف وقع ذلك عن نفسه وضمن نفقتهما وهو القياس؛ لأن كل واحد منهما أمره بتعيين الحج له، فإذا لم يعين فقد خالف فيضمن النفقة، وإن سكت عن ذكر المحجوج : معينا أو مبهما لا نص فيه من الأئمة، وينبغي أن يصح التعيين ههنا إجماعاً؛ لعدم المخالفة. (عيني، فتح) ودم الإحصار إلخ عند الطرفين، وقال أبو يوسف على المأمور؛ لأن دم الإحصار وجب للتحلل دفعا لضرر امتداد الإحرام، وهذا الضرر راجع إليه، ولهما: أن اللآمر هو الذي أدخله في هذه العهدة فعليه خلاصه، فإن كان الحج عن الميت فدم الإحصار في مال الميت عندهما خلافا له. (مستخلص) على المأمور: وكذا دم رفض النسك عليه، أما القرآن؛ فلأنه وجب شكرا للجمع بين النسكين، والمأمور هو المختص بهذه النعمة لوقوع الفعل منه، وأما دم الجناية؛ فلأنه الجاني فتجب الكفارة عليه، وصورة دم القران أن يأمره واحد بالقران أو يأمره اثنان أحدهما بالحج والآخر بالعمرة، وأذنا له بالقران وأما إذا فعل ذلك بغير إذن فيضمن النفقة. رمز الحقائق: ۱۸۷/۱] (فتح) فقد صار مخالفاً فإن مات المأمور بالحج أو سرقت نفقته. (ط، ع) عنه : أي عن الميت الأول الذي كان أوصى بالحج. (ع) من منزله فإن لم يكن له منزل فمن حيث مات اتفاقا. (ط)] وعندهما من حيث مات، وهذا الخلاف فيما إذا أطلق الوصية، أما إذا بين من أي مكان يحج عنه فمن ذلك الموضع بالإجماع، والخلاف فيه يبتني على خلافية أخرى، وهو إذا حج بنفسه ومات في الطريق، وأوصى بأن يحج عنه، فإنه يحج عنه من منزله عنده، وعندهما من موضع مات فيه وجه قوله وهو القياس أن القدر الموجود من السفر بطل في حق أحكام الدنيا؛ لقوله عليه: "كل عمل ابن آدم ينقطع بموته إلا ثلاثة ولد صالح الحديث، وتنفيذ الوصية من أحكام الدنيا، فوجب الاستئناف
Book of Hajj. Hajj on behalf of others only, and the condition is permanent incapacity until the time of death. And the condition of the incapacity of the one for whom hajj is performed is that it is not valid when he is able, for the obligatory (hajj), not the supererogatory. And whoever enters into ihram from [the one] with [the intention] does not have that, and it does not reach the deceased; because of His statement: 'And that man shall have nothing but what he strives for' (53:39). Malik and al-Shafi'i said: that is permissible in charity and financial worship and hajj, and not permissible in other acts of obedience like prayer, fasting, reciting Quran, etc. And for us: what is narrated that a man asked the Prophet (saw): "O Messenger of Allah! I had parents whom I honored during their lifetime, how can I honor them after their death?" The Prophet said: "Indeed, righteousness is that you pray for them with your prayer, and you fast with your fast," narrated by al-Daraqutni, meaning you give them the reward of your prayer and fasting. And what Mu'qil ibn Yasar narrated that he said: The Messenger of Allah (saw) said: "Recite Surah Ya Sin over your dead," narrated by Abu Dawud. And what is narrated that he (saw) sacrificed two horned rams, one for himself and the other for his ummah, agreed upon, meaning he gave the reward to his ummah. And what Anas narrated that he asked the Prophet (saw): "O Messenger of Allah! We give charity for our dead, and perform hajj for them, and supplicate for them; does that reach them?" He said: "Yes! It reaches them and they rejoice with it just as one of you rejoices with a tray when it is given to him," narrated by Abu Ja'far al-Askari. And the verse is abrogated by His statement: 'And those who believe and whose offspring follow them in faith, We will join their offspring with them' (52:21), so children are admitted due to the righteousness of fathers. Ibn Abbas said it abrogates it. And it is said: it is specific to the people of Moses and Abraham because it is a narration of what was in their scriptures in His statement: 'Or has he not been informed of what is in the scriptures of Moses and of Abraham who fulfilled?' (53:36-37). And it is said: by 'man' is meant the disbeliever, while the believer has what his brother strives for. And it is said: he does not have it by way of justice but has it by way of favor. And it is said: the lam (in 'li') means 'upon', as in His statement: 'and upon them is the curse' (40:52), and His statement: 'and if you do evil, then it is upon it' (17:7). [Symbol of al-Haqaiq: 186/1] (Fath) Himself only: meaning the condition of allowing deputyship in hajj (may Allah have mercy) until the time of death, [like chronic illness and amputation of legs. And if he has hajj performed for him while sick or imprisoned, then if he dies, it is permissible; if the excuse ceases, it becomes invalid. (T)] If the hajj is obligatory, i.e., it was incumbent upon him, and he was capable then became incapable after that. This according to Abu Hanifa. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is obligatory to make someone perform hajj for the incapable if he has wealth; so it is not required that it become obligatory upon him while healthy. So if he has someone else perform hajj then becomes incapable, it does not suffice him, and several have stated this explicitly. From here is derived the invalidity of what the sultans and ministers do of appointing deputies for themselves in hajj, because their incapacity is not continuous until death. The condition of continuous incapacity is because it is an obligation of a lifetime. So even if he has hajj performed for himself while sick, it is suspended; if he dies, it suffices; if he recovers, it becomes invalid, so the obligation of Hajj al-Islam remains upon him, and what was performed is supererogatory. Likewise, if he has hajj performed for himself while imprisoned. (Ayni, Fath) Al-manub (the one for whom hajj is performed): with damm on the mim, fat-ha on the nun, and kasra on the shadda waw, from al-tanwib meaning al-munib (the one deputizing). Not supererogatory: [because the field of supererogatory is wider, so it is permissible for a healthy capable person to have a man perform hajj with his wealth as a supererogatory act. (Miskin (T))] because in supererogatory hajj, deputyship is allowed even with capability; because the field of supererogatory is wider. Do you not see that supererogatory prayer is allowed sitting or riding even with the ability to stand and dismount? And the correct position in the school regarding the one who performs hajj for another is that the essence of the hajj falls on the one for whom it is performed; due to the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah who said: "O Messenger of Allah! The obligation of Allah regarding hajj caught my father as a very old man who cannot stay firm on a mount; should I perform hajj for him?" He said: "Yes," agreed upon. And from Muhammad (al-Shaybani) that the hajj falls on the pilgrim and the employer has the reward of the expenses, and the obligation of hajj is not removed from the deputy; rather it is a transfer, because it is not performed except with the intention of obligation or absolute intention, and that did not exist; only the intention for the employer existed. (Fath, Ayni) His two employers: that two men ordered him to perform hajj for each of them, so he entered ihram for both; then the hajj is for himself. [Symbol of al-Haqaiq: 187/1] He is liable for the expenses: because he disobeyed them, and the hajj does not fall for them but falls for himself. (T, A)] For his two employers, and it indicates that it does not fall for either of them; because each one only ordered him to make the intention specifically for him, and he cannot perform it for one of them due to lack of priority, so it falls for the agent. If he intended one without specifying, then if he continues on that, he becomes a disobeyer by agreement. If he specified one before tawaf and standing, as a transfer, from him, it is permissible according to both parties and falls for that one, and he is liable for the expenses for the second. According to Abu Yusuf, it falls for himself and he is liable for both expenses; and that is the analogy, because each of them ordered him to specify the hajj for him, and if he did not specify, he disobeyed so he is liable for the expenses. If he remained silent about mentioning the one for whom hajj is performed, whether specified or unspecified, there is no text from the imams. And it should be that specification here is valid by consensus, due to lack of disobedience. (Ayni, Fath) And the dam of ihsar (prevention) etc. is upon the employer according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad); and Abu Yusuf said upon the agent; because the dam of ihsar is obligatory for tahlul to ward off the harm of extended ihram, and this harm returns to him. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): the employer is the one who brought him into this responsibility, so he must release him. If the hajj is for a deceased, then the dam of ihsar is from the wealth of the deceased according to them, contrary to him (Abu Yusuf). (Mustakhlas) Upon the agent: likewise the dam of abandoning the ritual is upon him. As for qiran (combining 'umra and hajj), because it is obligatory as gratitude for combining the two rituals, and the agent is the one specifically enjoying this blessing because the action comes from him. As for the dam of transgression, because he is the transgressor, so the expiation is upon him. The scenario of dam of qiran is that one person orders him to do qiran, or two persons order him, one for hajj and the other for 'umra, and they permit him to do qiran. But if he does that without permission, he is liable for the expenses. Symbol of al-Haqaiq: 187/1] (Fath) So he has become a disobeyer. If the agent dies during hajj, or his expenses are stolen. (T, A) From him: meaning from the first deceased who had bequeathed the hajj. (A) From his home; if he has no home, then from where he died by agreement. (T)] And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), from where he died. This difference is when the bequest is absolute. If it is specified from which place to perform hajj for him, then from that place by consensus. And this difference is based on another difference, which is: if he performs hajj himself and dies on the way, and bequeaths that hajj be performed for him, then according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is performed for him from his home; according to them, from the place where he died. The face of his (Abu Hanifa's) statement, and it is the analogy, is that the portion of travel that occurred becomes void with respect to the rulings of this world, due to his (saw) statement: "Every action of the son of Adam is cut off by his death except three: a righteous child..." and the implementation of the bequest is from the rulings of this world, so restarting is obligated.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with the rulings of performing Hajj on behalf of another person (al-hajj 'an al-ghayr). It is an expansion on the conditions, the dispute regarding benefit to the deceased, and the detailed rulings concerning the agent (al-ma'mur). 

The passage begins by stating the core condition for valid representation in obligatory Hajj: the person on whose behalf it is performed must be permanently incapacitated until death. This incapacity must be continuous; temporary illness or imprisonment does not suffice unless it persists until death. The Hanafi school distinguishes between obligatory and supererogatory Hajj: for the former, representation is only valid when the principal is permanently unable; for the latter, representation is allowed even if the principal is capable, because the field of supererogatory acts is more flexible.

A major section addresses the dispute with Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i, who held that acts of worship like prayer, fasting, and Quran recitation cannot benefit the deceased, though charity, financial worship, and Hajj can. The Hanafi school argues that they do benefit, citing several hadiths: the Prophet (saw) instructed a man to pray and fast for his parents, told to recite Surah Ya Sin over the dead, sacrificed a ram for his ummah, and confirmed that charity, Hajj, and supplication reach the deceased. The verse "man shall have nothing but what he strives for" (53:39) is addressed in multiple ways: it is abrogated by the verse joining offspring with believing fathers (52:21); it is specific to the scriptures of Moses and Abraham; it refers to the disbeliever only; the believer benefits from others' acts by way of divine favor, not strict justice; or the preposition 'lam' means 'upon' (i.e., liability rather than benefit).

The passage then explains the condition further according to Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Hanifa, the obligation must have been incumbent upon the person while healthy, then he became permanently incapable. According to them, if an incapable person has wealth, he must hire someone to perform Hajj for him, even if the obligation did not arise while healthy. This leads to a practical critique: rulers and ministers who appoint deputies for themselves while they are capable and not permanently incapacitated are not fulfilling their obligation correctly.

The latter part of the passage (from 'al-sahih min al-madhhab') deals with the agent's rulings. The correct position is that the Hajj falls on the person for whom it is performed, based on the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah. Imam Muhammad holds that it falls on the pilgrim (agent), but the employer gets the reward of expenses. The passage then discusses a scenario where two employers hire one agent to perform Hajj for each. If the agent enters ihram for both, the Hajj is for himself and he must compensate the employers for expenses. If he intends one without specifying, he becomes a disobeyer. If he specifies one before tawaf and standing, it is valid for that one, and he compensates the other. According to Abu Yusuf, it falls for himself and he compensates both. The passage also covers who bears the dam (blood sacrifice) for ihsar (prevention), qiran (combining), and jinnayat (transgressions): generally, the employer bears it according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf places it on the agent. For a deceased principal, the dam is from the deceased's wealth. Finally, it discusses the case of the agent's death or theft of expenses, and the difference of opinion on where to perform the substitute Hajj when the deceased died en route: Abu Hanifa says from the deceased's home, while the two disciples say from the place of death.

Key Terms
المنوب (al-manūb): The person on whose behalf an act is performed, specifically the one for whom Hajj is performed (al-munīb).
المأمور (al-ma'mūr): The agent who is hired or commissioned to perform the act (here, Hajj).
دم الإحصار (dam al-iḥṣār): The blood sacrifice (dam) required when a pilgrim is prevented (muḥṣar) from completing Hajj or 'Umra.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the condition for performing obligatory Hajj on behalf of another person?
A) The person being represented must be unable to perform Hajj due to any temporary excuse, like illness.
B) The person being represented must be permanently incapacitated until death, and the incapacity must be continuous.
C) The person being represented must have sufficient wealth to hire a deputy.
D) The person being represented must have previously performed Hajj himself.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, representation in obligatory Hajj requires permanent incapacity until death; additionally, all acts of worship performed for the deceased benefit them according to strong hadith evidence.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Practical Rulings of Hajj on Behalf of Another
States specific financial and ritual liabilities in deputized Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who bears the expenses and dam (penalty) liabilities when performing hajj on behalf of another, and the rule if the agent dies en route.

Core Idea
Expenses and dam al-ihsar are on the commander; dam al-qiran and jinaya are on the agent.

Hajj on behalf of another involves multiple financial and ritual responsibilities. This lesson clarifies who guarantees the journey costs, who owes the various sacrificial penalties, and what happens if the agent dies during the journey. These details ensure that the arrangement is valid and just for both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
The 'commander' (amir) is the person on whose behalf hajj is performed; the 'agent' (ma'mur) is the one performing it.
2
Determine expenses
The text states 'al-hajj 'an al-ghayr 'an amirihi damina al-nafaqah' — the commander guarantees the expenses. So the commander must provide all travel costs.
This includes transportation, food, and accommodation.
3
Allocate dam liabilities
Dam al-ihsar (penalty for being prevented from completing Hajj) is on the commander. Dam al-qiran (for combining Hajj and Umrah) and dam al-jinayah (penalty for violations) are on the agent.
This is because the agent is the one performing the acts that may incur penalties.
4
Handle agent's death
If the agent dies en route, Hajj is performed on his behalf from his residence using one-third of what remains (of the expenses or his wealth). The text clarifies that even if the agent dies, the dam al-jinayah still applies because he was the one who committed the violation.
The 'one-third' refers to the portion of his estate available for bequests.

Source Text

الحج عن الغير عن آمريه ضمن النفقة، ودم الإحصار على الآمر ، ودمُ القران والجناية على المأمور، فإن مات في طريقه يُحجّ عنه من منزله بثلث ما بقي. الميت أي دم الجناية لأنه الجاني - والصحيح من المذهب في من عن غيره أن أصل الحج يقع عن المحجوج عنه؛ لحديث الخثعمية قالت: "يا رسول الله ! إن فريضة الله في الحج أدركت أبي شيخاً كبيراً لا يثبت على الراحلة أفأحج عنه؟" قال: "نعم"، متفق عليه، وعن محمد أن الحج يقع عن الحاج وللآمر ثواب النفقة، ولا يسقط فرض الحج عن النائب، بل يكون نقلا؛ لأنه لا يتأدى إلا بنية الفرض أو مطلق النية و لم توجد وإنما وجدت النية عن الآمر. (فتح عيني)
Hajj on behalf of another: Regarding the one who commands him, he guarantees the expenses. The blood of being prevented (ihsar) is upon the commander, and the blood of qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah) and of jinayah (penalty) is upon the commanded agent. If he dies on his way, Hajj is performed for him from his residence using one third of what remains. The deceased: i.e., the blood of jinayah because he is the perpetrator. And the correct view in the madhhab concerning one who performs Hajj for another is that the original Hajj falls on the one on whose behalf it is performed, due to the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah who said: 'O Messenger of Allah, the obligation of Hajj from Allah has overtaken my father who is a very old man and cannot sit firmly on the mount. Shall I perform Hajj on his behalf?' He said: 'Yes.' (Agreed upon). And from Muhammad that the Hajj falls on the pilgrim (the agent) and for the commander there is reward for the expenses. And the obligation of Hajj is not dropped from the deputy (na'ib); rather, it is a transfer (naql), because it cannot be performed except with the intention of obligation or absolute intention, and that did not occur; only the intention for the commander was found. (Fath al-'Ayni)
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with commentary presents the foundational ruling of Hajj on behalf of another. The matn states essential rules: the commander must provide expenses, dam al-ihsar is on the commander, dam al-qiran and dam al-jinayah are on the agent, and if the agent dies en route, a hajj is performed from his residence using one-third of remaining wealth. The correct view in the madhhab is that the original hajj falls on the commanded person, based on the hadith of Khath'amiyyah. The Prophet’s permission to perform Hajj for the elderly father establishes the validity and that the obligation is fulfilled for the one on whose behalf it is performed. Imam Muhammad holds that the hajj falls on the agent, with the commander receiving reward for expenses, and the agent's own obligation remains (it is a transfer, not fulfillment). The reasoning is that the agent’s intention was for the commander, not for his own obligation or absolute intention.

Key Terms
دم الإحصار (dam al-ihsar): The sacrificial animal due when a pilgrim is prevented from completing Hajj.
دم القران (dam al-qiran): Penalty for combining Hajj and Umrah without a break.
دم الجناية (dam al-jinayah): Penalty for violations during ihram, such as hunting or cutting trees.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the agent dies en route, from where is the Hajj performed and using what portion?
A) From the commander's residence using full expenses
B) From the agent's residence using one-third of what remains
C) From the nearest city using the commander's funds
D) The Hajj is cancelled and must be repeated

Key Takeaway
In deputized Hajj, expenses and dam al-ihsar fall on the commander; dam al-qiran and jinayah fall on the agent; if the agent dies en route, Hajj is performed from his estate using one-third.

The Ruling and Proof: Does Hajj Fall on the Commander or the Agent?
Presents the correct madhhab view with hadith proof and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the correct Hanafi view that the original hajj falls on the commanded person, cite the hadith of Khath'amiyyah as proof, and contrast Imam Muhammad's dissenting position.

Core Idea
The correct view: the hajj falls on the commanded person, proven by the Prophet's permission.

A key dispute within the Hanafi school concerns the effect of deputized Hajj: does the obligation fall on the commander (the one on whose behalf it is performed) or on the agent? This lesson presents the relied-upon view supported by the famous hadith of Khath'amiyyah, and explains Imam Muhammad's alternative reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the correct view (al-sahih)
The text declares: 'al-sahih min al-madhhab' — the correct view in the madhhab is that the original Hajj falls on the one on whose behalf it is performed (al-mahjuj 'anhu).
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Identify the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Khath'amiyyah, where a woman asks the Prophet ﷺ if she can perform Hajj for her elderly father. The Prophet replies 'Yes' (n'am).
The hadith is agreed upon (muttafaq 'alayh) by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's permission (amr) indicates that the Hajj performed on behalf of another fulfills the obligation of the commanded person. The woman's father was physically unable, and the Prophet validated the substitute.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub (a command indicates obligation).
4
Contrast Imam Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad holds that the Hajj falls on the agent (the actual pilgrim). The commander only gets reward for the expenses, and the agent's own obligation is not dropped; it is a transfer (naql), not fulfillment.
His reasoning: intention for the commander does not fulfill the agent's own fard.
5
Understand the rejection of Muhammad's view
The text says 'al-sahih min al-madhhab' implying the majority of the school (including Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) take the former view. Muhammad's view is marjuh (weaker) for fatwa.
The tarjih is based on the clear hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحج عن الغير عن آمريه ضمن النفقة، ودم الإحصار على الآمر ، ودمُ القران والجناية على المأمور، فإن مات في طريقه يُحجّ عنه من منزله بثلث ما بقي. الميت أي دم الجناية لأنه الجاني - والصحيح من المذهب في من عن غيره أن أصل الحج يقع عن المحجوج عنه؛ لحديث الخثعمية قالت: "يا رسول الله ! إن فريضة الله في الحج أدركت أبي شيخاً كبيراً لا يثبت على الراحلة أفأحج عنه؟" قال: "نعم"، متفق عليه، وعن محمد أن الحج يقع عن الحاج وللآمر ثواب النفقة، ولا يسقط فرض الحج عن النائب، بل يكون نقلا؛ لأنه لا يتأدى إلا بنية الفرض أو مطلق النية و لم توجد وإنما وجدت النية عن الآمر. (فتح عيني)
Hajj on behalf of another: Regarding the one who commands him, he guarantees the expenses. الصحيح من المذهب (al-sahih min al-madhhab): The correct or relied-upon position within the Hanafi school.
نقل (naql): A transfer; in this context, the concept that deputized hajj is a transfer of reward but not a fulfillment of the commander's obligation.

Two Commanders: Acting for Both – Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on specification in delegated hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi majority and Abu Yusuf's positions regarding the validity of specifying one of two commanders for hajj, and apply the rule on guarantee of expenses.

Core Idea
A single hajj cannot serve two commanders unless intention is specified before the key rites.

When two individuals commission the same person to perform hajj on their behalf, the agent cannot simultaneously fulfill both commands because exclusive intention is required for each. This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on such a scenario, focusing on the dispute between the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf. The key is whether the agent can salvage the hajj for one of them by specifying before the essential acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
Recognize that the agent assumes ihram for both commanders simultaneously. The baseline ruling is that the hajj falls for the agent himself.
This is because he cannot make exclusive intention for either.
2
Understand the majority position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad)
If the agent specifies one commander before tawaf and wuquf, the hajj becomes valid for that person. He must then guarantee the expenses for the second commander.
Specification before the key rites resolves the conflict.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that regardless of specification, the hajj always falls for the agent, and he must guarantee expenses for both commanders.
His reasoning is qiyas: each commander commanded specification, so failure to specify is a violation.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The text indicates that the majority view is relied upon ('jaza 'inda al-tarafayn'). Specification before tawaf and wuquf is valid and effective.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آمريه بأن أمره رجلان أن يحج عن كل منهما فأحرم عنهما فالحج له. [رمز الحقائق: ۱۸۷/۱] ضمن النفقة: الأنه خالفهما ولا يقع الحج عنهما بل يقع عن نفسه. (ط، ع)] لآمريه، وفيه إيماء إلى أنها لا تقع عن أحدهما؛ لأن كل واحد إنما أمره أن يخلص النية له ولا يمكنه الإيقاع عن أحدهما؛ لعدم الأولوية، فوقعت عن المأمور وإن نوى أحدهما غير عين فإن مضى على ذلك صار مخالفا بالاتفاق، وإن عين أحدهما قبل الطواف والوقوف عن جاز عند الطرفين ويقع عنه، ويضمن النفقة للثاني، وعند أبي يوسف وقع ذلك عن نفسه وضمن نفقتهما وهو القياس؛ لأن كل واحد منهما أمره بتعيين الحج له، فإذا لم يعين فقد خالف فيضمن النفقة، وإن سكت عن ذكر المحجوج : معينا أو مبهما لا نص فيه من الأئمة، وينبغي أن يصح التعيين ههنا إجماعاً؛ لعدم المخالفة. (عيني، فتح)
Two commanders: that two men command him to perform hajj for each of them, so he assumes ihram for both. Then the hajj is for himself. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/187). He guarantees the expenses because he disobeyed them, and the hajj does not fall for them but falls for himself. (Ta' and 'Ayn) For the two commanders, there is an indication that it does not fall for either of them, because each one commanded him to dedicate intention to him, and he cannot perform it for one due to lack of priority, so it falls for the agent. If he intends one of them without specification and continues, he becomes a violator by consensus. If he specifies one before tawaf and standing (wuquf), it is valid according to both parties and falls for that person, and he guarantees expenses for the second. According to Abu Yusuf, it falls for himself and he guarantees expenses for both, and that is the qiyas (analogy), because each one commanded him to specify the hajj for him, so if he did not specify, he has disobeyed and thus guarantees expenses. And if he remains silent about mentioning the person for whom the hajj is performed, whether specified or unspecified, there is no explicit text from the imams, but specification should be valid here by consensus due to absence of violation. ('Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where one person is commanded by two individuals to perform Hajj on behalf of each of them. If he assumes ihram for both at once, the hajj falls for himself, not for either commander, because he cannot fulfill the condition of exclusive intention for each. The text from Ramz al-Haqa'iq notes that he must guarantee expenses for both. If he intends one without specifying, he violates by consensus. However, if he specifies one before tawaf and wuquf, it is valid and falls for that person, but he must guarantee expenses for the second. Abu Yusuf holds that it falls for the agent himself, and he guarantees expenses for both, as this is the strict analogy (qiyas). If the agent is silent about the beneficiary, the text notes there is no explicit ruling from earlier imams, but specification should be valid by consensus. This showcases the Hanafi method of resolving conflicts between explicit command and practical possibility.

Key Terms
آمريه (aamirayn): Two persons commanding the same agent to perform hajj for each of them.
تخليص النية (takhlees al-niyyah): To make the intention exclusive for a specific person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hajj is invalid and he must start over
B) The hajj falls for the specified person, and he guarantees expenses for the second
C) The hajj falls for himself, and he guarantees expenses for both
D) The hajj falls for both commanders equally

Key Takeaway
A single hajj can only fulfill one commission if the agent specifies the beneficiary before tawaf and wuquf; otherwise it counts as the agent's own.

Liability for Blood Sacrifices in Deputized Hajj
Explains liability for blood sacrifices in deputized hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the liability for dam al-ihsar, dam al-qiran, and dam al-jinayah in deputized hajj and distinguish between the majority (the two) and Abu Yusuf's positions.

Core Idea
In deputized hajj, the commander bears dam al-ihsar; the agent bears dam al-qiran and dam al-jinayah.

When a person performs hajj on behalf of another, various blood sacrifices (dams) may become obligatory. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies who bears each dam: the agent (ma'mur) or the commander (amir). The ruling involves a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute, with the majority (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) holding the commander liable for dam al-ihsar, while Abu Yusuf alone argues for the agent's liability. Understanding the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind these assignments is key.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three dams and their categories
List the three blood sacrifices mentioned: dam al-ihsar (prevention), dam al-qiran (combining hajj and 'umrah), and dam al-jinayah (violation during ihram). Recognize that each has a different basis for obligation.
Dam al-ihsar is due to prevention, dam al-qiran as gratitude, dam al-jinayah as expiation.
2
Locate the majority ruling
From the phrase 'عند الطرفين' (according to the two), identify that the dominant Hanafi view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) places dam al-ihsar on the commander. Understand their reasoning: the commander brought the agent into this responsibility, so he must secure his release.
The two also rule that if hajj is for a deceased, dam al-ihsar is from the deceased's estate.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's contrary view
Abu Yusuf argues that dam al-ihsar is on the agent because the harm of prolonged ihram affects the agent personally. Compare this reasoning with the majority's.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
4
Apply the rules for dam al-qiran and dam al-jinayah
Note that both dams are on the agent: dam al-qiran as gratitude for the blessing of combining the rituals (the agent performed the actions), and dam al-jinayah because the agent committed the violation. Recognize the scenario for qiran: either one commander orders qiran, or two commanders order hajj and 'umrah separately and permit qiran.
If the agent performs qiran without permission, he must cover expenses.
5
Summarize the legal logic (ta'lil)
Identify the effective cause for each ruling: for dam al-ihsar, the commander's act of delegation; for dam al-qiran, the agent's specific blessing; for dam al-jinayah, the agent's act of violation. Recognize how these connect to the obligation.
The commentary uses explicit ta'lil: 'because' (لأن) statements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودم الإحصار إلخ عند الطرفين، وقال أبو يوسف على المأمور؛ لأن دم الإحصار وجب للتحلل دفعا لضرر امتداد الإحرام، وهذا الضرر راجع إليه، ولهما: أن اللآمر هو الذي أدخله في هذه العهدة فعليه خلاصه، فإن كان الحج عن الميت فدم الإحصار في مال الميت عندهما خلافا له. (مستخلص) على المأمور: وكذا دم رفض النسك عليه، أما القرآن؛ فلأنه وجب شكرا للجمع بين النسكين، والمأمور هو المختص بهذه النعمة لوقوع الفعل منه، وأما دم الجناية؛ فلأنه الجاني فتجب الكفارة عليه، وصورة دم القران أن يأمره واحد بالقران أو يأمره اثنان أحدهما بالحج والآخر بالعمرة، وأذنا له بالقران وأما إذا فعل ذلك بغير إذن فيضمن النفقة. رمز الحقائق: ۱۸۷/۱] (فتح)
And the blood of ihsar, etc., according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is on the commander, while Abu Yusuf says it is on the commanded agent, because dam al-ihsar becomes obligatory for the sake of tahlul (ending ihram) to remove the harm of prolonging ihram, and this harm reverts to him. While the two argue that the commander is the one who brought him into this responsibility, so upon him is his release. If the hajj is on behalf of a deceased, then dam al-ihsar is from the wealth of the deceased according to the two, contrary to him. (Mustakhlas) On the commanded agent: similarly, dam of abandoning the rites (rafd al-nusuk) is upon him. As for dam al-qiran, it became obligatory as gratitude for combining the two rituals, and the commanded agent is the one specifically endowed with this blessing because the action is from him. As for dam al-jinayah, because he is the perpetrator, so the expiation is obligatory on him. The scenario of dam al-qiran is that one person commands him to do qiran, or two command him, one for hajj and one for 'umrah, and they permit him to do qiran. But if he does that without permission, he guarantees the expenses. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/187) (Fath)
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage details the liability for various blood sacrifices (dams) in the context of hajj on behalf of another. The general rule from the matn is that dam al-ihsar is on the commander, while dam al-qiran and dam al-jinayah are on the agent. The commentary presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that dam al-ihsar is on the agent because the harm of being prevented affects him personally. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, here meaning the majority) argue that since the commander brought the agent into this endeavor, the commander is responsible for releasing him. If the hajj is for a deceased, the dam is from the deceased's estate according to the two, but Abu Yusuf disagrees. The text also clarifies that dam al-qiran is on the agent as a gratitude for the blessing of combining the two rituals, and dam al-jinayah is on the agent as he committed the violation. This showcases how Hanafi jurists assign responsibility based on effective cause (talil) and the intent behind the obligation.

Key Terms
دم الإحصار (dam al-ihsar): The blood sacrifice due when a pilgrim is prevented from completing the pilgrimage (e.g., by enemy or illness).
دم القران (dam al-qiran): The blood sacrifice for performing hajj and 'umrah together while in ihram.
دم الجناية (dam al-jinayah): The blood sacrifice for committing a violation (jinayah) during ihram, such as hunting or shaving before tahlul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The commander (amir)
C) The deceased's estate
D) The local mosque

Key Takeaway
In deputized hajj, the commander bears dam al-ihsar because he initiated the agency, while the agent bears dam al-qiran and dam al-jinayah because he performed the actions or committed the violation.

Where to Perform Hajj When the Agent Dies: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on performing hajj from which location when the agent dies en route

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the location of hajj when the agent dies en route, and apply the thuluth ma baqiya calculation in the given scenario.

Core Idea
When the hajj agent dies en route, Abu Hanifa requires a fresh start from the deceased's residence; the Sahibayn allow building upon the travel already done.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about executing a hajj bequest when the appointed agent dies or his funds are stolen. The disagreement hinges on a foundational principle: does the agent's death invalidate the journey in worldly terms? This leads to different practical outcomes in determining the starting point for the hajj and the calculation of available funds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and points of disagreement
Recall that the deceased bequeathed hajj; the agent either dies or the expenses are stolen. The dispute is whether the hajj should be performed from the deceased's residence (Abu Hanifa) or from where the agent died (Sahibayn).
The disagreement only applies when the bequest is absolute; if a specific place is named, all agree on that place.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's argument
Abu Hanifa argues that the agent's journey is invalidated in worldly rulings because deeds end at death (based on the hadith: 'Every son of Adam's deeds are cut off by his death except three...'). Since executing a bequest is a worldly matter, the hajj must start anew from the deceased's home.
This is a qiyas jaliy: the journey is analogous to deeds that stop at death.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's argument
The Sahibayn argue that the travel is not invalidated, citing Quran 4:100 and the statement of 'Ali that one who dies on the hajj path continues to receive rewards. Therefore, the remaining journey can be completed from where the agent died.
They prioritize spiritual continuity over the worldly legal principle.
4
Analyze the thuluth ma baqiya scenario
Work through the example: estate 4000 dirhams, hajj cost 1000. The executor gives 1000 to the agent, who then dies or the money is stolen. Apply each imam's method: Abu Hanifa takes one-third of what remains after the loss (of the allocated 1000); Muhammad uses the remaining allocated money; Abu Yusuf uses what remains of the original one-third of the estate plus any remaining allocated money.
This illustrates how the foundational dispute affects the financial calculation of the bequest.
5
Determine the practical thamarah
The practical difference is the starting point: Abu Hanifa's view may require a longer journey from the deceased's home, while the Sahibayn's view may allow a shorter journey from the agent's death place, potentially reducing costs.
The financial calculation in the example also shows varying amounts available for the hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن مات المأمور بالحج أو سرقت نفقته. (ط، ع) عنه : أي عن الميت الأول الذي كان أوصى بالحج. (ع) من منزله فإن لم يكن له منزل فمن حيث مات اتفاقا. (ط)] وعندهما من حيث مات، وهذا الخلاف فيما إذا أطلق الوصية، أما إذا بين من أي مكان يحج عنه فمن ذلك الموضع بالإجماع، والخلاف فيه يبتني على خلافية أخرى، وهو إذا حج بنفسه ومات في الطريق، وأوصى بأن يحج عنه، فإنه يحج عنه من منزله عنده، وعندهما من موضع مات فيه وجه قوله وهو القياس أن القدر الموجود من السفر بطل في حق أحكام الدنيا؛ لقوله عليه: "كل عمل ابن آدم ينقطع بموته إلا ثلاثة ولد صالح الحديث، وتنفيذ الوصية من أحكام الدنيا، فوجب الاستئناف ما بقي، ومن أهل بحج عن أبويه فعين صح. ووجه قولهما: أن من لم يبطل بموته؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ يَخْرُجُ مِنْ بَيْتِهِ مُهَاجِراً إِلَى اللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ثُمَّ يُدْرِكْهُ الْمَوْتُ فَقَدْ وَقَعَ أَجْرُهُ عَلَى اللَّهِ (النساء:۱۰۰) الآية، وقال علي: "من مات في طريق الحج كتب له حجة مبرورة في كل سنة"، فإذا لم يبطل عمله وجب البناء عليه، وقوله: "بثلث ما بقي صورته: رجل أوصى بأن يحج عنه ومات وترك أربعة ألاف درهم، وكان مقدار الحج ألف درهم فأخذ الوصي ألفاً ودفعها إلى الذي يحج عنه فمات، أو سرقت في الطريق منه، فعند أبي حنيفة: يؤخذ ثلث ما بقي من التركة بعد التلف، وعند محمد: يحج عنه بما بقي من المال المدفوع إليه المفرز للحج إن بقي شيء، وإلا بطلت الوصية، وعند أبي يوسف: يحج عنه بما بقي من الثلث الأول، وهو ثلاث مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث درهم مع ما بقي من المال المفرز إن بقي، وإن لم يبق فيما بقى من الثلث الأول. (فتح) ماله عند أبي حنيفة إن كان يكفي للحج من منزله وإلا فمن حيث يبلغ. (ط)
If the commanded agent for hajj dies, or his expenses are stolen. (Ta, 'Ayn) 'Anhu: i.e., from the first deceased who had bequeathed hajj. ('Ayn) From his residence; if he has no residence, then from where he died by agreement. (Ta) And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), from where he died. This dispute applies when the bequest is absolute. But if he specifies from which place to perform hajj for him, then from that place by consensus. This dispute is based on another difference: if he himself performed hajj and died on the way, and bequeathed that hajj be performed for him, then according to him (Abu Hanifa) hajj is performed for him from his residence, and according to the two from the place where he died. His (Abu Hanifa's) argument and that of qiyas is that the portion of travel that occurred is invalidated in the context of worldly rulings, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Every son of Adam's deeds are cut off by his death, except three: a righteous child, etc.' And executing a bequest is from worldly rulings, so starting anew is required. And the argument of the two is that the deed is not invalidated by his death, due to the verse: 'And whoever leaves his home as an emigrant to Allah and His Messenger, and then death overtakes him, his reward has already fallen upon Allah' (4:100), and 'Ali said: 'Whoever dies on the path of hajj, a blessed hajj is written for him every year.' So if his deed is not invalidated, building upon it is required. And his statement: 'using one third of what remains' – its scenario: a man bequeathed that hajj be performed for him, died, and left 4000 dirhams, and the amount for hajj was 1000 dirhams. The executor took 1000 and gave it to the one who would perform hajj for him, then that agent died or it was stolen on the way. According to Abu Hanifa: one third of what remains of the estate after the loss is taken. According to Muhammad: hajj is performed for him with what remains of the money given to him that was allocated for hajj, if anything remains; otherwise the bequest becomes void. According to Abu Yusuf: hajj is performed for him with what remains of the first third, which is 333 and one-third dirhams, plus what remains of the allocated money if anything remains; and if nothing remains of the first third, it is void. (Fath) According to Abu Hanifa, if it is sufficient for hajj from his residence, then [proceed], otherwise from where it reaches. (Ta)
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This dense passage covers the dispute about where to perform hajj when the appointed agent dies or his expenses are stolen. If the deceased had bequeathed hajj, Abu Hanifa holds that hajj should be performed from the deceased's residence (or from where he died if no residence), while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it should be performed from the place where the agent died. This difference applies when the bequest is absolute; if the deceased specified a location, that must be followed by consensus. The underlying disagreement is about the effect of the agent's death on his travel: Abu Hanifa argues that the journey is invalidated in worldly terms, so the hajj must start anew from the residence, analogizing to the hadith that deeds end at death. The two argue that the travel is not invalidated, citing the Quranic verse about the emigrant whose reward is secured, and the statement of 'Ali that one who dies on the hajj path continues to receive rewards. The passage then illustrates the 'thuluth ma baqiya' rule with a scenario: a man leaves 4000 dirhams, hajj cost 1000. The executor gives 1000 to the agent, who then dies or it is stolen. The three imams differ: Abu Hanifa takes one-third of what remains of the estate after the loss; Muhammad uses the remaining allocated money; Abu Yusuf uses what remains of the first third (the original 1/3 of estate). This shows the practical application of the dispute about where to begin the hajj.

Key Terms
ثلك ما بقي (thuluth ma baqiya): One-third of what remains of the estate after the loss or theft of the funds allocated for the hajj.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest; the instruction left by a deceased person for a charitable or religious act, such as hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One-third of the original 4000 dirhams (1333.33 dirhams)
B) One-third of what remains of the estate after the loss (1000 dirhams)
C) The remaining 3000 dirhams
D) Nothing, the bequest becomes void

Key Takeaway
When the hajj agent dies, Abu Hanifa requires the hajj to start from the deceased's residence and calculates the available funds as one-third of what remains of the estate after the loss.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Hajj for Parents without Command: Specification and Virtue
Ruling on performing hajj for parents without command, with specification and virtue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specifying a parent after performing hajj for both without command, and explain the distinction between fulfilling an obligation and dedicating reward.

Core Idea
A single hajj cannot be for two persons; without command, it is a reward dedication, not obligation transfer.

This lesson examines a common scenario: performing hajj intending it for both parents without their prior command. The Hanafi school clarifies that such an intention does not transfer the obligation; rather, it is a dedication of reward. However, the performer may later specify one parent, and the act itself is highly recommended. Understanding the difference between niyabah (substitute performance) and ihdah (reward dedication) is essential to correctly apply this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing hajj for both parents without their command, followed by specification to one parent. The ruling: the specification is valid absolutely, whether before or after wuquf and tawaf.
The key point is that the initial intention for both is null; the hajj remains as a cause for reward.
2
Understand the legal principle
A single hajj cannot fulfill the obligation for two persons. Therefore, intending it for both parents without command does not transfer the obligation to them; rather, it becomes a reward dedication.
The phrase 'نيته عنهما لغو' indicates that the intention for both is invalid.
3
Distinguish niyabah from ihdah
Niyabah (substitute hajj) requires the prior command or permission of the person being replaced, and it fulfills their obligation. Ihdah (dedication of reward) does not require permission and does not fulfill the obligation; it simply directs the reward to the intended person.
In this case, since there is no command, it is ihdah, not niyabah.
4
Recognize the recommendation and its evidence
Performing hajj for parents is mustahabb (recommended), supported by hadiths from Imam Ali and the Prophet (peace be upon him) that promise great reward.
The hadiths are quoted to encourage the act, not to establish obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أهل بحج عن أبويه فعين صح. أي مطلقا سواء كان قبل الوقوف والطواف أو بعدهما؛ لأن م حج عن غيره بغير أمره لا يكون حاجاً عنه، بل يكون جاعلاً ثواب حجه له ونيته عنهما لغو؛ لأن الحجة الواحدة لا تكون عن اثنين فيبقى أصل الحج وهو سبب للثواب، فله أن يجعله لأحدهما أو لهما، والحج عن الوالدين مستحب؛ لقوله علي: "من حج عن أبويه أو قضى عنهما مغرماً بعث يوم القيامة مع الأبرار"، وقوله عليه: أبيه أو أمه فقد قضى عنه حجته، وكان له فضل عشر حجج ، وقوله عليه: "إذا حج الرجل عن والديه فقبل منه ومنهما، واستبشرت أرواحهما وكتب عند الله براً ". (فتح)
And whoever performs hajj for his parents by declaring ihram, then later specifies one, it is valid. i.e., absolutely, whether before the standing (wuquf) and tawaf or after them. Because one who performs hajj for another without his command is not performing hajj for him; rather, he is making the reward of his hajj for him, and his intention for both is null, since a single hajj cannot be for two persons. Thus the original hajj remains, which is a cause for reward, so he may assign it to one of them or to both. And performing hajj for parents is recommended (mustahabb), due to the saying of 'Ali: 'Whoever performs hajj for his parents or pays off a debt for them will be raised with the righteous on the Day of Judgment,' and his saying (peace be upon him): 'If a man performs hajj for his father or mother, he has fulfilled his hajj, and for him is the reward of ten pilgrimages,' and his saying (peace be upon him): 'When a man performs hajj for his parents, it is accepted from him and from them, and their souls rejoice, and he is recorded with Allah as righteous.' (Fath)
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a person performs hajj intending it for both his parents without being commanded by them. The ruling is that if he later specifies one parent (either before tawaf and wuquf or after), it is valid. The reason is that performing hajj for another without command does not transfer the hajj to that person; rather, it is as if the performer is dedicating its reward. A single hajj cannot be for two persons simultaneously, so the intention for both is null. The hajj remains valid as a cause for reward, and the performer may assign its reward to one or both parents. The passage also highlights that hajj for parents is mustahabb (recommended), supported by traditions from 'Ali and the Prophet (peace be upon him) emphasizing the great reward.

Key Terms
جاعلاً ثواب حجه له (jaa'ilan thawaba hajjihi lahu): Dedicating the reward of the hajj to someone else, not transferring the actual obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, it is valid at any time
B) Only before wuquf
C) Only before tawaf
D) No, the hajj is invalid

Key Takeaway
A single hajj cannot be for two persons; without command, the performer retains the right to dedicate its reward to one or both parents at any time.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Wasiyyah for Hajj: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wasiyyah for Hajj after loss of funds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on funding Hajj from a bequest when the designated funds are lost, and apply each position to a given scenario.

Core Idea
When designated Hajj funds are lost, Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad disagree on which portion of the estate is used — a case study in intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about fulfilling a bequest for Hajj when the allocated money is lost. The three founding imams offer differing solutions, each based on a principle of balancing the bequest with heirs' rights. Understanding their reasoning sharpens your ability to trace legal derivations within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Recognize the problem: a man bequeaths Hajj, leaves 4000 dirhams, allocates 1000 for Hajj. The proxy dies or money is stolen. Now how to fund the Hajj?
The key is that the specific allocated money is lost.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Abu Hanifa: take one-third of what remains of the entire estate after the loss (i.e., from the remaining 3000, take 1000 for Hajj).
He considers the bequest a charge on the estate as a whole.
3
State Muhammad's Position
Muhammad: use whatever remains of the specifically allocated 1000 for Hajj; if nothing remains, the bequest becomes void.
He restricts the bequest to the designated fund.
4
State Abu Yusuf's Position
Abu Yusuf: use what remains of the original one-third (i.e., 333.33 dirhams) plus any remaining allocated money; if the original third is exhausted, nothing else.
He splits the difference, prioritizing the third set aside for wasiyyah.
5
Compare the Practical Outcome (Thamarah)
Apply each position to the same scenario: Abu Hanifa takes 1000 from the estate, Muhammad takes 0 if the 1000 is gone, Abu Yusuf takes up to 333.33 plus whatever remains of the 1000.
The different outcomes affect the heirs' shares significantly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما بقي، ومن أهل بحج عن أبويه فعين صح. أي أحرم بعد ذلك لأحدهما خروجه كأنه لم يوجد الخروج، أو خرج بغير حج فأوصى أن يحج عنه، فيحج عنه بلده، ووجه قولهما: أن من لم يبطل بموته؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ يَخْرُجْ مِنْ بَيْتِهِ مُهَاجِرًا إِلَى اللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ثُمَّ يُدْرِكْهُ الْمَوْتُ فَقَدْ وَقَعَ أَجْرُهُ عَلَى اللَّهِ﴾ [النساء:100]، وقال علي: "من مات في طريق الحج كتب له حجة مبرورة في كل سنة"، فإذا لم يبطل عمله وجب البناء عليه، وقوله: "بثلث ما بقي صورته: رجل أوصى بأن يحج عنه ومات وترك أربعة آلاف درهم، وكان مقدار الحج ألف درهم فأخذ الوصي ألفاً ودفعها إلى الذي يحج عنه فمات، أو سرقت في الطريق منه، فعند أبي حنيفة: يؤخذ ثلث ما بقي من التركة بعد التلف، وعند محمد: يحج عنه بما بقي من المال المدفوع إليه المفرز للحج إن بقي شيء، وإلا بطلت الوصية، وعند أبي يوسف: يحج عنه بما بقي من الثلث الأول، وهو ثلاث مائة وثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث درهم مع ما بقي من المال المفرز إن بقي، وإن لم يبق في ما بقى من الثلث الأول. (فتح) ماله عند أبي حنيفة إن كان يكفي للحج من منزله وإلا فمن حيث يبلغ. (ط) ما بقي: من . عن من أبويه : من . . غير أمرهما ولم يعين. (ط) صح: أي مطلقا سواء كان قبل الوقوف والطواف أو بعدهما؛ لأن من حج عن غيره بغير أمره لا يكون حاجاً عنه، بل يكون جاعلاً ثواب حجه له ونيته عنهما لغو؛ لأن الحجة الواحدة لا تكون عن اثنين فيبقى أصل الحج وهو سبب للثواب، فله أن يجعله لأحدهما أو لهما، والحج عن الوالدين مستحب؛ لقوله علي: "من حج عن أبويه أو قضى عنهما مغرماً بعث يوم القيامة مع الأبرار"، وقوله عليه: "من حج عن أبيه أو أمه فقد قضى عنه حجته، وكان له فضل عشر حجج"، وقوله عليه: "إذا حج الرجل عن والديه فقبل منه ومنهما، واستبشرت أرواحهما وكتب عند الله براً". (فتح) "من حج عن
What remains, and whoever enters ihram for Hajj on behalf of his parents and specifies, it is valid. That is, he entered ihram after that for one of them, his departure as if it did not occur, or he departed without Hajj and bequeathed that Hajj be performed for him, then it is performed for him from his town. And the evidence of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that one whose act is not invalidated by his death, due to His saying, Exalted: 'And whoever leaves his home emigrating to Allah and His Messenger and then death overtakes him, his reward has already become incumbent upon Allah' [4:100], and Ali said: 'Whoever dies on the path of Hajj, a perfect Hajj is recorded for him every year.' Since his deed is not invalidated, building upon it is obligatory. And his saying: 'From the third of what remains' — its scenario: a man bequeathed that Hajj be performed for him and died, leaving four thousand dirhams, and the amount for Hajj was one thousand dirhams. The executor took one thousand and gave it to the one who was to perform Hajj for him, then the latter died, or it was stolen from him on the way. According to Abu Hanifa: the third of what remains of the estate after the loss is taken. According to Muhammad: Hajj is performed for him with what remains of the money given and allocated for Hajj, if anything remains; otherwise the bequest becomes void. According to Abu Yusuf: Hajj is performed for him with what remains of the first third, which is three hundred and thirty-three and one-third dirhams, along with what remains of the allocated money if any; if nothing remains of the first third, (then from the rest). (Fath) His wealth according to Abu Hanifa: if it suffices for Hajj from his home, then from there; otherwise from where it reaches. (T) 'What remains' from... 'from his parents' — i.e., he did not seek their permission and did not specify. (T) 'Valid' means absolutely, whether before standing at Arafah and tawaf or after; because whoever performs Hajj for another without his permission is not performing Hajj on his behalf, but rather makes the reward of his Hajj for him, and his intention for both is futile; because one Hajj cannot be for two persons, so the original Hajj remains as a cause for reward, and he can assign it to one or both of them. Hajj for one's parents is recommended due to the saying of Ali: 'Whoever performs Hajj for his parents or repays a debt for them will be raised on the Day of Judgment with the righteous', and his saying: 'Whoever performs Hajj for his father or mother has fulfilled his Hajj obligation for him, and he will have the reward of ten Hajjs', and his saying: 'When a man performs Hajj for his parents, it is accepted from him and from them, their souls rejoice, and he is recorded as righteous with Allah.' (Fath) 'Whoever performs Hajj for...'
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute within a broader ruling on Hajj on behalf of others. The author of Kanz al-Daqaiq (a Hanafi matn) states that if a person enters ihram for Hajj on behalf of his parents without their permission and later specifies one of them, it is valid. The commenter expands: specification can be before or after the pillars. The core ruling: Hajj for another without permission makes the reward transferable to that person, but the Hajj is the performer's own; he cannot intend for two simultaneously. Then a detailed case on wasiyyah (bequest) for Hajj: a man leaves 4000 dirhams, bequeaths Hajj for 1000, the executor gives 1000 to a proxy, but the proxy dies or the money is stolen. The three Hanafi imams differ:
- Abu Hanifa: take one-third of what remains of the estate after the loss (i.e., from the remaining 3000, take 1000, so 2000 left for heirs).
- Muhammad al-Shaybani: use whatever remains of the specifically allocated 1000; if nothing remains, the bequest is void.
- Abu Yusuf: use what remains of the original one-third (i.e., 333.33 dirhams) plus any remaining allocated money; if the first third is exhausted, nothing.
The text also cites Quran 4:100 and a Hadith from Ali to support that Hajj is not invalidated by death, so building upon the intention is required. The passage ends with recommendations for Hajj on behalf of parents, citing multiple narrations.

Key Terms
حج عن الغير (Hajj 'an al-Ghayr): Performing Hajj on behalf of another person, with or without their permission; without permission, the Hajj is for the performer but reward can be gifted.
الوصية بالحج (al-Wasiyyah bil-Hajj): A bequest requiring Hajj to be performed for the deceased from one-third of his estate.
ثلث ما بقي (Thuluth ma Baqi): One-third of what remains of the estate after a loss (e.g., theft or death of proxy). Used in Abu Hanifa's ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the wasiyyah case where the proxy dies or money is stolen, what is the position of Abu Hanifa?
A) Hajj is performed only if the specific allocated money remains.
B) One-third of what remains of the entire estate after the loss is used for Hajj.
C) The bequest becomes void entirely.
D) Hajj is performed from the remaining one-third of the original third.

Key Takeaway
In intra-Hanafi disputes, the difference often hinges on the source of funds for bequests, reflecting broader principles of balancing the deceased's intent with heirs' rights.
